```
                                                                                                              4: \mathbf{return} \ \mathsf{smsg}_2 = (c_{\mathsf{mac}}, z_{\mathsf{os}}, z_{\mathsf{mac}}, z_{\mathsf{dleq}})
Algorithm \mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{Ver}(\mathsf{pp},\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{info},\mu,\sigma)
1: parse \sigma = (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1), \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}})
 2: \quad (D_2, D_3) \leftarrow \mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}(\mathsf{info}) \; ; \mathtt{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}} = (D_1, D_2, D_3)
 3: \mathbb{X}_{os} \leftarrow W; \mathbb{X}_{mac} \leftarrow (\mathsf{ipp}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}); \mathbb{X}_{rnd} \leftarrow (W, \widetilde{A}_{os}, \mathsf{cmt}_{rnd}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)
4: \quad \mathbf{return} \ \widetilde{U} \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}} \ \land \ (\forall \mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\} : \varSigma_{\mathsf{xxx}}.\mathsf{Ver}(\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}}) = 1)
                        \wedge \ (\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{mac}} + \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}) = \mathsf{H}(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mu, \mathsf{info})
 5:
```

<span id="page-17-1"></span>**Fig. 5.** Setup, key generation, and signer-side algorithms of the three-move blind signature scheme  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}} = \mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}[\mathsf{GGen},\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}},\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}},\mathsf{H},\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}]$  and  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}} = \mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}[\mathsf{GGen},\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}]$ . Here,  $\mathsf{H}:\{0,1\}^* \to \mathbb{Z}_p^3$  and  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}:\{0,1\}^* \to \mathbb{G}^2$ . Recall that  $(\mathbb{G},p,G) \leftarrow \mathsf{GGen}(1^\lambda)$  is an implicit input for all algorithms. We omitted the input state for  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{Sign}_2$ , assuming that this algorithm can access values from the prior round.

#### <span id="page-17-0"></span>3.2 Construction

We now describe our blind signature construction in Figure 5 (the signer-side algorithms) and Figure 6 (the user-side algorithms). The secret key sk consists of the  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  secret key msk and the Okamoto-Schnorr witness  $\boldsymbol{w} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  with the public key containing the corresponding issuer parameters ipp and  $W = \phi_{\mathsf{pp},W}^{\mathsf{os}}(\boldsymbol{w})$ .

In the signing protocol, the signer computes the  $\Sigma_{os}$  nonce  $A_{os}$ , uses msk to compute its tag  $\sigma_{mac} = (U, V, S, T)$ , and computes the nonces for the OR-proof between (a)  $\Sigma_{mac}$ , which proves that  $\sigma_{mac}$  satisfies certain structure in Equation (2) with respect to ipp and  $A_{os}$ , and (b)  $\Sigma_{dleq}$ , which proves that  $(D_2, D_3)$  (computed by hashing the common message info) has the same discrete logarithm with respect to the bases  $(G, D_1)$  in pp (this side is simulated). The user then blinds the  $M_{alg}$  tag along with the nonces while proving knowledge (via  $\Sigma_{rnd}$ ) of the blinding factors  $(\alpha_{os}, \gamma_{os}, r_x, r_y, r_M)$  (committed to via  $C_{rnd}$ ) for  $A_{os}$  and  $\sigma_{mac}$ . The user then hashes the blinded tag and nonces to obtain the challenges  $(\tilde{c}_{os}, \tilde{c}_{or}, \tilde{c}_{rnd})$ , respectively for  $\Sigma_{os}$ , the OR-proof between  $\Sigma_{mac}$  and  $\Sigma_{dleq}$ , and  $\Sigma_{rnd}$ , which are blinded and sent to the signer. The signer finalizes its side by computing the corresponding responses. The user finally computes the signature by blinding the responses.

Remark 3.3 (Properties and Optimizations). We remark some desirable properties of  $BS_{alg}$ . First, the setup algorithm is transparent (the setups of  $C_{mac}$  and  $C_{rnd}$  are transparent in our instantiations), and can be generated (alternatively) by simply hashing a fixed string as with some prior blind signatures works [KRS23, KR25]. Also, as with many existing signatures from Fiat-Shamir paradigm and canonical  $\Sigma$ -protocols (e.g.,

<span id="page-17-2"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>4</sup> Notably, we need to embed these blinding factors with base  $\widetilde{U}$  due to a technical step in the OMSUF proof—we further expand on this in Section 3.3

{18}------------------------------------------------

```
\operatorname{Algorithm}\ \mathsf{BS}_{\operatorname{alg}}.\mathsf{U}_1(\mathsf{pp},\mathsf{vk},\mathsf{info},\mu\in\{0,1\}^{\bigstar},\mathsf{smsg}_1=(A_{\operatorname{os}},A_{\operatorname{mac}},A_{\operatorname{dleq}},\sigma_{\operatorname{mac}}=(U,V,S,T))):
  1: if U = 0_{\mathbb{G}} then abort
   2: (D_2, D_3) \leftarrow \mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}(\mathsf{info}) \; ; \mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}} \leftarrow (D_1, D_2, D_3)
               \gamma_{os}, \gamma_{mac}, \gamma_{dleq} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p // Challenge blinding factors
   3:
  4: \alpha_{os} = (\alpha_0, \alpha_1) \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2, \alpha_{mac} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^6 \times C_{mac}.\mathcal{R}, \alpha_{dleq} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p // Response blinding factors
  5: \beta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*, r_x, r_y, r_M \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p // MAC tag blinding factors
  6: \widetilde{A}_{os} \leftarrow A_{os} + \alpha_0 G + \alpha_1 H - \gamma W // Blind Okamoto-Schnorr nonce
  7: \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}} \leftarrow A_{\mathsf{dleq}} + \alpha_{\mathsf{dleq}} \cdot (G, D_2) - \gamma_{\mathsf{dleq}}(D_1, D_3) // Blind DLEQ nonce
  8: \widetilde{M} \leftarrow A_{os} + r_M F; \widetilde{U} \leftarrow \beta U; \widetilde{V} \leftarrow \beta V // Blind DDH-MAC tag
  9: \ \widetilde{S}_0 \leftarrow \beta S - r_r \widetilde{U} : \widetilde{S}_1 \leftarrow r_r G + r_M X_1
10: \tilde{T}_0 \leftarrow \beta T - r_u \tilde{U}; \tilde{T}_1 \leftarrow r_u G + r_M Y_1
11: \mathbf{x}'_{\text{mag}} = (\mathsf{ipp}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)
12: A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[V] \leftarrow \beta A_{\mathsf{mac}}[V] // Blind \Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}} nonces
13: A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[S_1] \leftarrow A_{\mathsf{mac}}[S_1] + r_M A_{\mathsf{mac}}[X_1] + r_x A_{\mathsf{mac}}[G]
14: A'_{\text{mac}}[T_1] \leftarrow A_{\text{mac}}[T_1] + r_M A_{\text{mac}}[Y_1] + r_y A_{\text{mac}}[G]
15: A'_{\text{mac}} \leftarrow (A_{\text{mac}}[\text{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G], A'_{\text{mac}}[V, S_1, T_1])
16: \quad \widetilde{A}_{\text{mac}} \leftarrow A_{\text{mac}}' + \phi_{\text{pp}, x_{\text{mac}}'}^{\text{mac}}(\alpha_{\text{mac}}) \quad -\gamma_{\text{mac}}(\text{ipp}, G, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)
17: \rho_{\mathsf{rnd}} \leftarrow \mathbb{S} \mathbb{Z}_p \; ; \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}} \leftarrow \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{bck}, ( \alpha_0 \widetilde{U}, \alpha_1 \widetilde{U} , \gamma_{\mathsf{os}} \widetilde{U} , r_x \widetilde{U}, r_y \widetilde{U}, r_M \widetilde{U} , A_{\mathsf{os}}); \rho_{\mathsf{rnd}})
18: \quad \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{rnd}} \leftarrow (W, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1) \; ; \; \mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{rnd}} \leftarrow (\rho_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \alpha_0, \alpha_1, \gamma_{\mathsf{os}}, r_x, r_y, r_M, A_{\mathsf{os}})
19: (\widetilde{A}_{rnd}, st_{rnd}) \leftarrow \Sigma_{rnd}.Init(pp, x_{rnd}) // Prove knowledge of blinding factors
20: \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} \leftarrow (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)
21: \quad (\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{or}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{H}(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mu, \mathsf{info})
22: \quad \mathbf{return} \ \mathsf{umsg} = (c_{\mathsf{os}} = \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}} - \gamma_{\mathsf{os}} \ , c_{\mathsf{or}} = \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{or}} - \gamma_{\mathsf{mac}} - \gamma_{\mathsf{dleq}} \ )
Algorithm \mathsf{BS}_{\mathrm{alg}}.\mathsf{U}_2(\mathsf{smsg}_2 = (c_{\mathsf{mac}}, z_{\mathsf{os}}, z_{\mathsf{mac}}, z_{\mathsf{dleq}})):
 1: c_{\text{dleq}} \leftarrow c_{\text{or}} - c_{\text{mac}}
 2: assert \forall xxx \in \{ \text{os, mac, dleq} \} : \Sigma_{xxx}. \text{Ver}(x_{xxx}, A_{xxx}, c_{xxx}, z_{xxx}) = 1
 3: \quad \widetilde{z}_{\text{os}} \leftarrow z_{\text{os}} + \alpha_{\text{os}} \quad ; \widetilde{z}_{\text{dleq}} \leftarrow z_{\text{dleq}} + \alpha_{\text{dleq}}
  4: \widetilde{c}_{\text{dleq}} \leftarrow c_{\text{dleq}} + \gamma_{\text{dleq}}; \widetilde{c}_{\text{mac}} \leftarrow c_{\text{mac}} + \gamma_{\text{mac}}
 5: \widetilde{z}_{\text{mac}} \leftarrow (\beta^{-1} z_{\text{mac}}[u], z_{\text{mac}}[z, x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, \rho_0]) + \alpha_{\text{mac}}
  6: \ \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}} \leftarrow \Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Resp}(\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}})
 7: return \sigma = (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}})
```

**Fig. 6.** User-side algorithms of the blind signature scheme  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  with the state for  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{U}_2$  omitted, assuming that this algorithm can access values from the prior round. We denote by  $A_{\mathsf{mac}}[\mathsf{xxx}]$  the component of  $A_{\mathsf{mac}}$  that corresponds to value xxx. That is,  $A_{\mathsf{mac}}[\mathsf{cmt}_0] = (A_{\mathsf{mac},1},\ldots,A_{\mathsf{mac},\ell_{\mathcal{C}}}), A_{\mathsf{mac}}[X_1] = A_{\mathsf{mac},\ell_{\mathcal{C}}+1}, A_{\mathsf{mac}}[Y_1] = A_{\mathsf{mac},\ell_{\mathcal{C}}+2},$  and so on, where  $\ell_{\mathcal{C}}$  the dimension of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathcal{C}$ . We follow the same convention for  $\widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . For readability, we highlight blinding of challenge, responses and MAC-related terms by  $\mathsf{mac}$ , and  $\mathsf{mac}$ , respectively.

{19}------------------------------------------------

Schnorr signatures [Sch90]), the nonces  $\widetilde{A}_{xxx}$  in our signature can be efficiently reconstructed from the statement  $x_{xxx}$ , the challenge  $\widetilde{c}_{xxx}$ , and the response  $\widetilde{z}_{xxx}$  (see the notations in BS.Ver in Figure 5). This allows us to reduce the signature size significantly by omitting the nonces in the derived signature. Additionally, if the scheme is to be used only as a (non-partially) blind signature scheme, the first move of the signer can be completely preprocessed.

#### <span id="page-19-0"></span>3.3 Correctness and Security

In this section, we establish correctness and concrete security guarantees for one-more strong unforgeability and partial blindness of  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  in the following theorems. The correctness proof is given in Section 5, the OMSUF proof is given in Section 6, while the partial blindness proof is given in Section 7.

<span id="page-19-2"></span>**Theorem 3.4 (Correctness).** Let GGen be a group parameters generator outputting groups of prime-order  $p = p(\lambda)$ ,  $C_{mac}$ ,  $C_{rnd}$  be commitment schemes,  $M_{alg} = M_{alg}[GGen, C_{mac}]$  be the algebraic MAC scheme described in Section 3.1, and H,  $H_{pb}$  be random oracles. Let  $BS_{alg} = BS_{alg}[GGen, C_{mac}, C_{rnd}, H, H_{pb}]$ . The blind signature  $BS_{alg}$  is perfectly correct.

Proof (Sketch). This follows from straightforward calculation. In particular,  $\tilde{U} \neq 0$  and the hash verification query are immediate. The transcript  $(\tilde{A}_{rnd}, \tilde{c}_{rnd}, \tilde{z}_{rnd})$  is computed from a witness  $w_{rnd}$  such that  $(x_{rnd}, w_{rnd}) \in \mathfrak{R}_{rnd}$  and is therefore valid. Note that the signer-issued  $\Sigma_{os}$  transcript  $(A_{os}, c_{os}, z_{os})$  is computed with witness  $w_{os}$  such that  $(x_{os}, w_{os}) \in \mathfrak{R}_{os}$  and the signer-issued  $\Sigma_{dleq}$  transcript  $(A_{dleq}, c_{dleq}, z_{dleq})$  is simulated for  $x_{dleq}$ . Further, observe that the blinded  $\Sigma$ -protocols transcripts  $(\tilde{A}_{xxx}, \tilde{c}_{xxx}, \tilde{z}_{xxx})$  for  $xxx \in \{os, dleq\}$  are obtained by the user running Rand specified in Lemma 2.18 on the signer-issued transcripts  $(A_{xxx}, c_{xxx}, z_{xxx})$ . Thus, these transcripts remain valid by Definition 2.16. The  $\Sigma_{mac}$  transcript requires more calculation and we refer to the full proof for details. Roughly, we mimic the blinding of  $\sigma_{mac}$  on the  $\Sigma$ -protocol transcript to adapt  $\tau_{mac} = (A_{mac}, c_{mac}, z_{mac})$  into a valid transcript for  $\tilde{\sigma}_{mac}$ , leveraging the linear structure of  $\Sigma_{mac}$ . These steps are highlighted with  $\overline{\phantom{a}}$  in Figure 6. The adapted transcript is valid for the blinded MAC  $\tilde{\sigma}_{mac}$  and is randomized via Rand as the other transcripts.

<span id="page-19-1"></span>**Theorem 3.5 (One-More Strong Unforgeability).** Let  $(\mathsf{GGen}, p, \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}, \mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}})$  be as in Theorem 3.4, and  $\mathsf{H}, \mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$  be random oracles. Assume also that  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$  is perfectly strong binding and  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  satisfies extractability.

For any adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  running in time  $T_{\mathcal{A}} = T_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$ , making at most  $Q_{S} = Q_{S}(\lambda)$ ,  $Q_{H} = Q_{H}(\lambda)$ , and  $Q_{pb} = Q_{pb}(\lambda)$  queries to oracles  $S_{1}$ , H, and  $H_{pb}$ , respectively, there exist adversaries  $\mathcal{B}_{ur,xxx}$  (for  $xxx \in \{os, mac, rnd\}$ ),  $\mathcal{B}_{dist}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}_{ddh,k}$  (for  $k \in [4]$ ),  $\mathcal{B}_{hide}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$  and  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  such that

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}}^{\mathsf{omsuf}}(\mathcal{A},\lambda) \leqslant \frac{1 + Q_{\mathsf{pb}}(Q_{\mathsf{H}}^2 + 12Q_{\mathsf{H}} + 3Q_{\mathsf{S}} + 4)}{p} + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur,os}},\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{sbind}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur,mac}},\lambda) \\ + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}}^{\mathsf{sbind}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur,rnd}},\lambda) + Q_{\mathsf{pb}} \cdot \left(\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}},\mathsf{Ext}}^{\mathsf{ext}-\mathsf{dist}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dist}},\lambda) + 2\sqrt[3]{32Q_{\mathsf{H}}^2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dl}},\lambda)} \right. \\ + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen},Q_{\mathsf{pb}}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},1},\lambda) + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen},Q_{\mathsf{S}}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},2},\lambda) + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{hide}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{hide}},\lambda) \\ + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},3},\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},4},\lambda) + \sqrt{Q_{\mathsf{H}} \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}}^{\mathsf{hide}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{alg}},\lambda)} \right) \; . \end{split}$$

Additionally, all adversaries runs in time roughly  $T_A$ , except for  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$  and  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  with running time roughly  $3T_A$  and  $2T_A$ , respectively. Moreover,  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  makes  $Q_S$  queries to its Tag oracle.

Proof (Detailed sketch). Our proof first move to a game that (a) guesses the common message info\* that A will forge on (via a guessing argument and hence the  $Q_{pb}$ -factor loss) and (b) extracts (via extractability of  $C_{rnd}$ ) the group elements committed to via  $\operatorname{cmt}_{rnd}$  of all forgeries, including the elements  $(\overline{A}_0, \overline{A}_1, \overline{\Gamma}_{os}, \overline{R}_x, \overline{R}_y, \overline{R}_M)$ , which embed the blinding factors in their exponents to basis  $\widetilde{U}$ , and the underlying Okamoto-Schnorr nonce  $\overline{A}_{os}$ . This induces the two following cases on collision of the extracted original nonces  $\overline{A}_{os}$  as discussed in Section 1.1.

{20}------------------------------------------------

Case 1: A pair of extracted  $\overline{A}_{os}$  collide. We consider two sub-cases.

- The two corresponding forgeries share the same RO query in their verification. We rely on (relaxed) unique responses properties of all the underlying  $\Sigma$ -protocols to extract hard to compute witnesses of  $\widetilde{\mathfrak{R}}_{os}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathfrak{R}}_{mac}$ , and  $\widetilde{\mathfrak{R}}_{rnd}$ , and ultimately reduce to DL and strong binding of  $\mathsf{C}_{mac}$  and  $\mathsf{C}_{rnd}$ . We remark that this step is crucial for strong unforgeability. For OMUF, the messages which are inputs to H are distinct, so this case never occurs.
- The two corresponding forgeries do not share the same RO query. Intuitively, the blinding factors  $\alpha_{os} = (\alpha_0, \alpha_1), \gamma_{os}$  embedded in the extracted  $(\overline{A}_0, \overline{A}_1, \overline{\varGamma}_{os})$  of the two forgeries will allow us to obtain two (unblinded)  $\Sigma_{os}$  transcripts with the same nonce  $\overline{A}_{os}$ . These determine a witness  $\boldsymbol{w}'$  that an be efficiently computed upon rewinding. Before rewinding and extracting these blinding factors, we make two key steps to ensure that (a) the unblinded challenges for the two transcripts are distinct which allows us to apply the special-soundness extractor, and that (b) we extract a different witness  $\boldsymbol{w}' \neq \boldsymbol{w}$  of W with sufficiently high probability. To see this more clearly, let  $(\widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{os}, \widetilde{z}_{os})$  and  $(\widetilde{A}'_{os}, \widetilde{c}'_{os}, \widetilde{z}'_{os})$  be the blinded transcripts from these two signatures and  $(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_{os}, \gamma_{os})$  and  $(\boldsymbol{\alpha}'_{os}, \gamma'_{os})$  be the corresponding blinding factors.

For (a), observe that the unblinded nonces being identical means

$$\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}} - \gamma_{\mathsf{os}} = \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{os}} - \gamma'_{\mathsf{os}}$$
.

With  $\tilde{c}_{os}$ ,  $\tilde{c}'_{os}$  being outputs of the random oracle H, this correlation only occurs with negligible probability (since  $\gamma_{os}$  and  $\gamma'_{os}$  are fixed when the queries are made). For (b), we employ similar statistical argument as in [PS00, TZ23, HKL19]. Essentially, we show that the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  is identical between the game using  $\boldsymbol{w} = (w_0, w_1)$  or  $\boldsymbol{w}' = (w_0 - \mathsf{dlog}_G H, w_1 + 1)$  to simulate the  $\Sigma_{os}$  part of the protocol. This allows us to argue that any (even unbounded) adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ , the witness  $\boldsymbol{w}'$  to W that it finds will be distinct from the one the game uses at least half of the time.

The above arguments allow us to argue that upon rewinding, the extracted witness w' is distinct from the witness w employed to simulate the signing oracles. Therefore, we can recompute the discrete logarithm of H via w and w' which breaks DL. (Note that  $dlog_G(H)$  is not required for simulation.)

Case 2: Extracted  $\overline{A}_{os}$  are distinct. Our goal in this case is to reduce to the UF-RMA security of  $M_{alg}$ . The proof is more complex than sketched in Section 1.1 due to partial blindness. We elaborate; the proof goes through the following steps.

- Set up H while knowing  $h = \mathsf{dlog}_G H$  and compute Okamoto-Schnorr nonce while knowing  $\mathsf{dlog}_G A_{\mathsf{os}} = r_{\mathsf{os},0} + r_{\mathsf{os},1} h$ .
- Simulate the MAC tags for sessions that do not sign the guessed common message info\* (identified with the initially guessed  $H_{pb}$ -query index). In particular, compute the tag as  $\sigma_{mac} = (U = uF, V = uZ, S \leftarrow \mathbb{G}, T \leftarrow \mathbb{G})$ . This change is due to an observation that  $(U, x_0U, y_0U)$  (where  $x_0U, y_0U$  are computed in the computation of S, T, respectively) is a DDH tuple with respect to the base  $(G, x_0G, y_0G)$ . To give the reduction to DDH (where  $x_0, y_0$  are not known), we have to (1) generate  $(D_2, D_3) = H(\text{info})$  with  $(D_2, D_3) = a(G, D_1)$  for some  $a \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , and (2) simulate  $\Sigma_{\text{mac}}$  and honestly compute  $\Sigma_{\text{dleq}}$  for the signing using the witness a. (Note that this is done to all sessions.)
- To enforce the structure check on  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}$  in the following bullet point, we have to switch  $\mathsf{H}(\mathsf{info}^*)$  back to uniformly random, and accordingly honestly compute  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  while simulating  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  during the signing of  $\mathsf{info}^*$ . (Note that the simulation of signing  $\mathsf{info} \neq \mathsf{info}^*$  is still identical to the previous step.)
- The game then enforces a structure check based on the linear map  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, x_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}$  (Eq. 2) on the MAC tags  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)$  and  $\widetilde{M}$  from  $\mathcal{A}$ 's signature outputs using  $\mathsf{msk}$ . This is possible through soundness of the OR-proof  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}} \vee \Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$ , since  $(D_2^*, D_3^*) = \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{info}^*)$  is still uniformly random so  $(D_1, D_2^*, D_3^*) \notin \mathfrak{L}_{\mathsf{dleq}}$ . In particular, if  $(\mathsf{ipp}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}) \notin \mathfrak{L}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ , the adversary can only output a valid  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}} \vee \Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  proof with negligible probability.
- The proof now (1) switches  $\mathsf{H}(\mathsf{info}^*)$  to  $(D_2^*, D_3^*) = a^*(G, D_1)$  for  $a \in \mathbb{Z}_p$  and (2) simulates all signing sessions by honestly running  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  with the witness and simulating  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Note that we have to maintain

<span id="page-20-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>5</sup> In the formal proof in Section 6, we introduce this step much earlier (before the extraction), but note that it is only required in this case.

{21}------------------------------------------------

the structure checks introduced in the previous steps, and more importantly they have to be efficient due to a DDH reduction to switch  $\mathsf{H}(\mathsf{info}^*)$ . This step is the reason why we need to commit to the blinding factors with base  $\widetilde{U}$  as naively checking (Eq. 2) requires knowing  $\mathsf{dlog}_G\widetilde{U}$ . The efficient check using  $\mathsf{msk}$  is:

$$\widetilde{V} = z\widetilde{U}$$
,  $\widetilde{S}_0 + \overline{R}_x = x_0\widetilde{U} + x_1C_M$ ,  $\widetilde{T}_0 + \overline{R}_y = y_0\widetilde{U} + y_1C_M$ ,

where  $C_M = (\operatorname{dlog}_G \widetilde{U}) \cdot \overline{A}_{os}$  is efficiently computable from the transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{os}, \widetilde{z}_{os}), h, \boldsymbol{w} = (w_0, w_1)$  and the extracted  $\overline{A}_0, \overline{A}_1, \overline{\Gamma}_{os}$ . Intuitively, this check ensures that  $(\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0 + \overline{R}_x, \widetilde{T}_0 + \overline{R}_y)$  is a valid tag for  $\overline{A}_{os}$ . For more detail, we refer to the proof in Section 6.3.

• Finally, we prepare for the rewinding by generating all the  $A_{os}$  nonces and their corresponding tags in advance so as to avoid tagging additional nonces during rewinding (as alluded to in Section 1.1). Then, we use the UF-RMA oracle to generate these prepared nonces and tags. At the end, we rewind  $\mathcal{A}$  to extract the blinding factor to obtain  $m^* = \mathsf{dlog}_G \overline{A}_{os}$ . We also recompute the unblinded tag  $\sigma^*_{\mathsf{mac}}$  for  $m^*$  from the blinding factors and  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Together,  $m^*$  and  $\sigma^*_{\mathsf{mac}}$  constitute a UF-RMA forgery (cf. Remark 3.2).

We show that  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  is partially blind if  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  is hiding in the random oracle model. Note that if  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  is perfectly hiding, then  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  satisfies  $\mathsf{statistical}$  partial blindness.

**Theorem 3.6 (Partial Blindness).** Let (GGen, p,  $C_{mac}$ ,  $C_{rnd}$ ,  $BS_{alg}$ ,  $M_{alg}$ ) be as in Theorem 3.4, and H,  $H_{pb}$  be random oracles. Assume that  $C_{mac}$  is perfectly binding. For any adversary A running in time  $T_A = T_A(\lambda)$ , making at most  $Q_H = Q_H(\lambda)$  and  $Q_{pb} = Q_{pb}(\lambda)$  queries to oracles H and  $H_{pb}$ , respectively, there exist adversary B running in time roughly  $T_A$ , such that

<span id="page-21-0"></span>
$$\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{rnd}}_{\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}}(\mathcal{A},\lambda) \leqslant \frac{2Q_{\mathsf{H}}}{p^3} + \frac{Q_{\mathsf{pb}} + 2}{p} + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{hide}}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}}(\mathcal{B},\lambda).$$

*Proof (Sketch).* We employ the framework of randomizable transcripts for canonical  $\Sigma$ -protocols from [KR25]. Roughly, we go through the following hybrids, starting from the original blindness game.

- We simulate the  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}})$  as usual: the game samples a random challenge  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ , uses the SHVZK simulator to simulate the nonce-response pair  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}})$  for  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ , and programs the random oracle H in the third slot with challenge  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  accordingly.
- We simulate the transcript  $(A_{os}, \tilde{c}_{os}, \tilde{z}_{os})$  and program H in the first slot with  $\tilde{c}_{os}$ , as above. Prior, the transcript was obtained by randomizing the (potentially maliciously-generated) transcript  $(A_{os}, c_{os}, z_{os})$  via the randomization algorithm from Lemma 2.18. As the transcript  $(A_{os}, c_{os}, z_{os})$  must verify due to the user-side check, the properties of the randomization algorithm (in particular Corollary 2.17) ensure that the distribution of  $(\tilde{A}_{os}, \tilde{c}_{os}, \tilde{z}_{os})$  remains identical.
- The transcripts of both branches of the OR-proof (i.e.,  $(\widetilde{A}_{mac}, \widetilde{c}_{mac}, \widetilde{z}_{mac})$  and  $(\widetilde{A}_{dleq}, \widetilde{c}_{dleq}, \widetilde{z}_{dleq})$ ) are simulated and  $\widetilde{c}_{or} = \widetilde{c}_{mac} + \widetilde{c}_{dleq}$  is programmed into the second slot of H. The distribution does not change with a similar argument to the above. Here, it is important that the modifications to the  $\Sigma_{mac}$  transcript  $(A_{mac}, c_{mac}, z_{mac})$ , due to the blinding of  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}$ , retain validity of the transcripts. (The latter is shown in the formal proof of Theorem 3.4.)
- We commit to the zero vector over  $\mathbb{G}^7$  in cmt<sub>rnd</sub>. As the  $\Sigma_{rnd}$  transcript is simulated, we can reduce to hiding of the commitment scheme  $C_{rnd}$ .

At this point, we do not require any computational assumptions anymore; the following modifications are inefficient but statistically indistinguishable.

• The game aborts if the adversarially-issued tag  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  does not follow the structure induced by  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, x_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}$ . To perform the (inefficient) check, the game brute-forces the secret key  $\mathsf{msk} = (x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z, \rho_0)$  for  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  (which is unique by perfect binding of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ ) and verifies that the MAC has the desired structure. For this step, it is important to note that the transcript  $(A_{\mathsf{mac}}, c_{\mathsf{mac}}, z_{\mathsf{mac}})$  functions as interactive proof that  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  has the desired structure. Then, the claim follows from 2-special soundness of both  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  and  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleg}}$ , as  $(D_1, \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{info}))$  is not a DDH-tuple except for negligible probability.

{22}------------------------------------------------

• Now, we compute the blinded MAC  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}$  and  $\widetilde{M}$  as follows

$$u \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*$$
,  $\widetilde{M} \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$ ,  
 $\widetilde{U} \leftarrow uG$ ,  $\widetilde{V} \leftarrow uzG$ ,  
 $\widetilde{S}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$ ,  $\widetilde{S}_0 \leftarrow u(x_0G + x_1\widetilde{M} - \widetilde{S}_1)$ ,  
 $\widetilde{T}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$ ,  $\widetilde{T}_0 \leftarrow u(y_0G + y_1\widetilde{M} - \widetilde{T}_1)$ .

Due to the above abort condition, the distribution of the blinded MAC remains identical.

Note that at this point, the view of the adversary is independent from the secret bit. This concludes the proof.

Remark 3.7 (ROM-free blindness). We still program the random oracle H in our blindness proof. Indeed, for an arbitrary hash function H, the scheme is not statistically blind. For instance, an inefficient adversary may choose info such that  $(D_1, \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{info}))$  is a DDH-tuple and then issue a malformed tag  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  in one session, and a valid tag in the other. Indeed, the blinded outputs will retain the structure of the tags, leading to a trivial (but inefficient) attack.

This can be remedied as follows. We let the signer issue an additional interactive proof that  $\sigma_{\text{mac}}$  is well-formed with an info-independent OR-branch, e.g., a fixed (non-)DDH-tuple  $D \leftarrow \mathbb{G}^3$ . This allows to simulate the interactive proof in the OMUF analysis, plus it is statistically hard to issue malformed MACs. Also, for the  $\Sigma_{\text{rnd}}$  proof, we can employ witness-indistinguishability if the commitment scheme is statistically hiding, which avoids programming the oracle H. We note that there are still some steps that rely on programming H, but these seem to be proof artifacts. Indeed, it is likely that a direct analysis of the distributions of blinded transcripts gives statistical blindness outside the ROM, akin to the analysis in [PS00, TZ22, CATZ24].

### <span id="page-22-0"></span>4 Instantiations

In this section, we present our two instantiations for compact signatures and statistical blindness (in the ROM).

#### <span id="page-22-1"></span>4.1 Compact Signatures

COMMITMENT SCHEMES FOR COMPACT SIGNATURES. For our compact instantiation that achieves computational blindness, we instantiate  $C_{rnd}$  with a multi-input ElGamal commitment, denoted  $C_{elg}$ , with message space  $\mathbb{G}^7$ . Similarly, we instantiate  $C_{mac}$  with  $C_{elg}$  for  $\mathbb{Z}_p^2$  messages as well (the commitment commits to  $(a,b) \in \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  by committing to  $(aG,bG) \in \mathbb{G}^2$ ). We present in Figure 7 the scheme with general message space  $\mathbb{G}^\ell$ . Lemma 4.1 establishes the security properties of  $C_{elg}$ . Namely, the properties of ElGamal encryption implies additive homomorphism, perfectly strong binding, extractability, and hiding (with the concrete bound implied from [BBKS07]).

<span id="page-22-2"></span>**Lemma 4.1.** Let GGen be a group parameter generator for groups of prime-order  $p = p(\lambda)$ . The commitment scheme  $C_{elg} = C_{elg}[GGen]$  as given in Figure 7 satisfies:

- 1. Linear-homomorphism.
- 2. Perfect strong binding.
- 3. Extraction with the extraction key identically distributed to C<sub>elg</sub>.Setup.
- 4. Computational hiding from DDH: For any adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  running in time  $T_{\mathcal{A}} = T_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$ , there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  running in time  $\approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that  $\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{hide}}_{\mathsf{Celg}}(\mathcal{A},\lambda) \leqslant 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ddh}}_{\mathsf{GGen}}(\mathcal{B},\lambda) + \frac{1}{2^{\lambda-2}}$ .

<u>Security.</u> The following corollary follows from Theorems 3.1 and 3.4 to 3.6 and lemma 4.1 along with DDH random self-reducibility (e.g., [EHK+13]).

Corollary 4.2 (Security of  $BS_{alg}$  with  $C_{elg}$ .). Let  $BS_{elg} = BS_{alg}[GGen, C_{elg}, C_{elg}, H, H_{pb}]$ . Then,  $BS_{elg}$  is perfectly correct, one-more strongly unforgeable, and computationally partially blind, under the DDH assumption.

{23}------------------------------------------------

**Fig. 7.** Multi-input ElGamal commitment for  $C_{elg}$ . $\mathcal{M} = \mathbb{G}^{\ell}$  along with its extraction algorithms Ext =  $(C_{elg}.ExtSetup, C_{elg}.Extract)$ 

```
 \begin{array}{llllllllllllllllllllllllllllllllllll
```

**Fig. 8.** Groth-Sahai commitment for message space  $C_{gs}$ . $\mathcal{M}=\mathbb{G}$  and  $\mathbb{G}^{\ell}$  along with its extraction algorithms  $Ext=(C_{gs}.ExtSetup,C_{gs}.Extract)$ .

EFFICIENCY. The first move of the signing protocol incurs  $1\mathbb{G}$  for  $A_{\text{os}}$ ,  $10\mathbb{G}$  for  $A_{\text{mac}}$ ,  $2\mathbb{G}$  for  $A_{\text{dleq}}$ , and  $4\mathbb{G}$  for  $\sigma_{\text{mac}}$ . The second move only requires  $2\mathbb{Z}_p$  elements. The third move requires  $2\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $z_{\text{os}}$ ,  $8\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $c_{\text{mac}}$ ,  $z_{\text{mac}}$ , and  $2\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $c_{\text{dleq}}$ ,  $z_{\text{dleq}}$ . This counts to  $17\mathbb{G} + 14\mathbb{Z}_p$  elements being sent in one protocol execution. The signature (ignoring the nonces as they can be reconstructed) contains  $7\mathbb{G}$  elements for  $(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\text{mac}})$ ,  $8\mathbb{G}$  for  $\text{cmt}_{\text{rnd}}$ ,  $14\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $(\widetilde{c}_{\text{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\text{xxx}})_{\text{xxx}\in\{\text{os},\text{mac},\text{dleq}\}}$ , and  $8\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $(\widetilde{c}_{\text{rnd}}, \widetilde{z}_{\text{rnd}})$ . In total, our signature size is  $15\mathbb{G} + 22\mathbb{Z}_p$ .

### <span id="page-23-0"></span>4.2 Statistical Blindness

COMMITMENT SCHEMES FOR STATISTICAL BLINDNESS. We use Groth-Sahai commitments [GS08], denoted  $C_{gs}$ , to individually commit to each group element as described in Figure 8. For  $C_{mac}$ , we use  $C_{elg}$  for  $\mathbb{Z}_p^2$  messages as in the prior construction, since the hiding property of  $C_{elg}$  does not affect blindness. The following lemma establishes the required properties for  $C_{gs}$ . We defer the proof to ??.

<span id="page-23-3"></span>**Lemma 4.3.** Let GGen be a group parameter generator for groups of prime-order  $p = p(\lambda)$ . The commitment scheme  $C_{gs} = C_{gs}[GGen]$  as given in Figure 8 satisfies:

- 1. Linear-homomorphism.
- 2. Computational strong binding from DL: For any adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  running in time  $T_{\mathcal{A}} = T_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$ , there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  running in time  $\approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that  $\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{sbind}}_{\mathsf{Celg}}(\mathcal{A}, \lambda) \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{dlog}}_{\mathsf{GGen}}(\mathcal{B}, \lambda)$ .
- 3. Extraction with extraction key computationally indistinguishability: For any adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  running in time  $T_{\mathcal{A}} = T_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$ , there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  running in time  $\approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that  $\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ext-dist}}_{\mathsf{Celg},\mathsf{Ext}}(\mathcal{A},\lambda) \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ddh}}_{\mathsf{GGen}}(\mathcal{B},\lambda)$ .
- 4. Statistical hiding: For any A,  $Adv_{C_{elg}}^{hide}(A, \lambda) \leq \frac{1}{p}$ .

*Proof.* We show the lemma for messages of length  $\ell=1$ , since the scheme for messages of length  $\ell>1$  simply commits to each element independently. Note that additive homomorphism, extraction, and statistical hiding is already implied by [GS08] adapted to pairing-free settings. Note that due to  $C_{gs}$ . Setup generating ck uniformly, there is a 1/p probability that (B,C)=b(G,A) for some  $b\in\mathbb{Z}_p$ , which makes ck not perfectly hiding constituting to the 1/p advantage.

{24}------------------------------------------------

Strong binding follows from observing that if two openings  $(M, \rho = (\rho_0, \rho_1)) \neq (M', \rho' = (\rho'_0, \rho'_1))$  are valid for some cmt  $\in \mathbb{G}^2$ . Then, we have that

$$0^2_{\mathbb{G}} = \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{gs}}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{ck}, M - M'; \rho - \rho') = \begin{pmatrix} 0 \\ M - M' \end{pmatrix} + \begin{pmatrix} G \ A \\ B \ C \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \rho_0 - \rho_0' \\ \rho_1 - \rho_1' \end{pmatrix} \ .$$

Observe that there are two cases: (1)  $\rho \neq \rho'$ , meaning  $(\rho_0 - \rho'_0)G + (\rho_1 - \rho'_1)A = 0$  so  $\mathsf{dlog}_G A = (\rho_0 - \rho'_0)(\rho_1 - \rho'_1)^{-1}$  can be computed. (2)  $\rho = \rho'$  and  $M \neq M'$ , which cannot occur, since it implies M = M'. Thus, a simple reduction can be computed.

SECURITY. The following corollary follows from Theorems 3.1 and 3.4 to 3.6 and lemma 4.3 along with DDH random self-reducibility (e.g., [EHK+13]).

Corollary 4.4 (Security of  $BS_{alg}$  with  $C_{gs}$ .). Let  $BS_{stat} = BS_{alg}[GGen, C_{mac} = C_{elg}, C_{rnd} = C_{gs}, H, H_{pb}]$ . Then,  $BS_{elg}$  is perfectly correct, one-more strongly unforgeable under the DDH assumption, and statistically partially blind.

EFFICIENCY. The signing protocol requires communicating  $17\mathbb{G} + 14\mathbb{Z}_p$  elements as with the compact instantiation, since  $C_{rnd}$  does not affect the communication. The signature contains  $7\mathbb{G}$  elements for  $(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{mac})$ ,  $14\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $(\widetilde{c}_{xxx}, \widetilde{z}_{xxx})_{xxx\in\{os, mac, dleq\}}$  (similar to before), and  $14\mathbb{G}$  for  $cmt_{rnd}$  (committing to  $7\mathbb{G}$  elements) and  $21\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $(\widetilde{c}_{rnd}, \widetilde{z}_{rnd})$ . In total, our signature size is  $21\mathbb{G} + 35\mathbb{Z}_p$ .

# <span id="page-24-0"></span>5 Correctness Proof of BS<sub>alg</sub>

We show Theorem 3.4, i.e., that  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  is correct. Recall that  $\mathsf{mpp} = (F, \mathsf{mck}), \, \mathsf{pp} = (\mathbb{G}, p, G, H, \mathsf{mpp}, \mathsf{bck}, \, \mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}}), \, \mathsf{msk} = (x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z, \rho_0) \, \text{and ipp} = (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z).$  Denote by

$$\sigma = (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}})$$

the output of a honest signing session. We need to show that

- $\widetilde{U} \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}$ ,
- $(\widetilde{c}_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{mac} + \widetilde{c}_{dleq}, \widetilde{c}_{rnd}) = \mathsf{H}(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}, \operatorname{cmt}_{rnd}, \widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{A}_{mac}, \widetilde{A}_{dleq}, \widetilde{A}_{rnd}, \mu, \operatorname{info}), \text{ and }$
- the Fiat-Shamir proofs verify.

We have  $u, \beta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*$  and  $\widetilde{U} = \beta U = (\beta u)G$ . Thus  $\widetilde{U} \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}$ . Also,  $c_{\mathsf{or}} = c_{\mathsf{dleq}} + c_{\mathsf{mac}}$  as chosen in  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{Sign}_2$ , therefore we have as desired that

$$\widetilde{c}_{\rm mac} + \widetilde{c}_{\rm dleq} = c_{\rm mac} + \gamma_{\rm mac} + c_{\rm dleq} + \gamma_{\rm dleq} = c_{\rm or} + \gamma_{\rm mac} + \gamma_{\rm dleq} = \widetilde{c}_{\rm or}.$$

Below, we focus on the Fiat-Shamir proofs  $\tilde{\tau}_{xxx} := (\tilde{A}_{xxx}, \tilde{c}_{xxx}, \tilde{z}_{xxx})$  for statements  $x_{xxx}$ , where  $xxx \in \{\text{os, mac, dleq, rnd}\}$ . The transcripts  $\tilde{\tau}_{xxx}$  are computed based on  $\Sigma$ -protocol transcripts  $\tau_{xxx} = (A_{xxx}, c_{xxx}, z_{xxx})$  issued by the signer as follows:

OKAMOTO-SCHNORR. The signer sets  $\mathbb{x}_{os} = W$  and  $\mathbb{w}_{os} = w$  in  $\mathsf{BS}_{alg}.\mathsf{KeyGen}$ . Note that  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp},\mathbb{x}_{os}}^{\mathsf{os}}(\mathbb{w}_{os}) = W$  by design. The signer sets  $(A_{\mathsf{os}},\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{os}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{E}_{\mathsf{os}}.\mathsf{Init}(\mathsf{pp},W,w)$  in  $\mathsf{BS}_{alg}.\mathsf{Sign}_1$ . Next, in  $\mathsf{BS}_{alg}.\mathsf{Sign}_2$ , the signer sets  $z_{\mathsf{os}} \leftarrow \varSigma_{\mathsf{os}}.\mathsf{Resp}(\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{os}}, c_{\mathsf{os}})$  with  $c_{\mathsf{os}} \in \mathbb{Z}_p$  supplied by the user. By correctness of  $\varSigma_{\mathsf{os}}$ , we have that  $(A_{\mathsf{os}}, c_{\mathsf{os}}, z_{\mathsf{os}})$  is valid for  $\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{os}}$ . The user derives the transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{os}})$  from  $(A_{\mathsf{os}}, c_{\mathsf{os}}, z_{\mathsf{os}})$  via Rand as specified in Lemma 2.18. Therefore, also  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{os}})$  is valid for  $\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{os}}$  by Definition 2.16.

DLOG EQUALITY. The signer simulates the transcript  $(A_{\mathsf{dleq}}, c_{\mathsf{dleq}}, z_{\mathsf{dleq}})$  for statement  $\mathbbm{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}} = (D_1, D_2, D_3)$ , where  $c_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  is provided by the user. Thus,  $(A_{\mathsf{dleq}}, c_{\mathsf{dleq}}, z_{\mathsf{dleq}})$  is valid for statement  $\mathbbm{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}}$ . As above, the user derives the transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{dleq}})$  from  $(A_{\mathsf{dleq}}, c_{\mathsf{dleq}}, z_{\mathsf{dleq}})$  via Rand from Lemma 2.18. In particular, the transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{dleq}})$  remains valid for  $\mathbbm{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  as Rand satisfies Definition 2.16.

{25}------------------------------------------------

MAC VALIDITY. The signer sets  $x_{\text{mac}} \leftarrow (\text{ipp}, A_{\text{os}}, U, V, S, T, 0_{\mathbb{G}}, 0_{\mathbb{G}})$  and  $w_{\text{mac}} \leftarrow (u^{-1}, \text{msk})$ , where  $\text{msk} = (x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z, \rho_0)$ . The transcript  $\tau_{\text{mac}}$  is computed via  $(A_{\text{mac}}, \text{st}_{\text{mac}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{E}_{\text{mac}}.\text{Init}(\text{pp}, x_{\text{mac}}, w_{\text{mac}})$  and  $z_{\text{mac}} \leftarrow \Sigma_{\text{mac}}.\text{Resp}(\text{st}_{\text{mac}}, c_{\text{mac}})$ , where  $c_{\text{mac}} \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Observe that  $u^{-1} \cdot U = G$  and as  $S = u(x_0G + x_1M)$ , it holds that  $x_0G + x_1M = u^{-1}S$  (similarly for  $y_0G + y_1M = u^{-1}T$ ). In addition, (msk, ipp) is setup honestly by the signer in BS<sub>alg</sub>. KeyGen, therefore we have  $\phi_{\text{mpp},x_{\text{mac}}}^{\text{mac}}(w_{\text{mac}}) = (\text{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G, V, 0_{\mathbb{G}}, 0_{\mathbb{G}})^{\mathsf{T}}$  (cf. Equation (2)). By correctness of  $\Sigma_{\text{mac}}$ , we obtain

$$\phi_{\mathsf{mpp}, \mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}(z_{\mathsf{mac}}) = A_{\mathsf{mac}} + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \cdot (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G, V, 0_{\mathbb{G}}, 0_{\mathbb{G}})^{\mathsf{T}}.$$

Note that  $\beta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*, r_x, r_y, r_M \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and the MAC randomized as described in Section 3.1 by the user. That is, we have  $\widetilde{U} = \beta U$ ,  $\widetilde{V} = \beta V$ ,  $\widetilde{M} = A_{os} + r_M F$ , and

$$\widetilde{S}_0 \leftarrow \beta S - r_x \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{S}_1 \leftarrow r_x G + r_M X_1,$$

$$\widetilde{T}_0 \leftarrow \beta T - r_y \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{T}_1 \leftarrow r_y G + r_M Y_1.$$

Following the notation in Figure 6, we next show that  $(A'_{\mathsf{mac}}, c, \beta^{-1} z_{\mathsf{mac}}[u], z_{\mathsf{mac}}[z, x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, \rho_0])$  is a valid transcript for statement  $\mathbf{x}'_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\mathsf{ipp}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)$  below, where  $A'_{\mathsf{mac}} = (A_{\mathsf{mac}}[\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G], \beta A_{\mathsf{mac}}[V], A_{\mathsf{mac}}[S_1] + r_M A_{\mathsf{mac}}[X_1] + r_x A_{\mathsf{mac}}[G], A_{\mathsf{mac}}[T_1] + r_M A_{\mathsf{mac}}[Y_1] + r_y A_{\mathsf{mac}}[G].$ 

$$\begin{split} \phi_{\mathsf{mpp}, \mathsf{z}'_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}(\beta^{-1} z_{\mathsf{mac}}[u], z_{\mathsf{mac}}[z, x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, \rho_0]) \\ & = \begin{pmatrix}
