c_{\mathsf{mac}}\mathsf{cmt_0} \\ a_{\mathsf{cmt_0}] + c_{\mathsf{mac}}\mathsf{cmt_0} \\ a_{\mathsf{cmt_$$

{26}------------------------------------------------

$$= \begin{pmatrix} A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \cdot (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G)^{\mathsf{T}} \\ \beta \ A_{\mathsf{mac}}[V] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \ \beta \ V \\ A_{\mathsf{mac}}[S_1] + r_M A_{\mathsf{mac}}[X_1] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} r_M X_1 + r_x (A_{\mathsf{mac}}[G] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} G) \\ A_{\mathsf{mac}}[T_1] + r_M A_{\mathsf{mac}}[Y_1] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} r_M Y_1 + r_y (A_{\mathsf{mac}}[G] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} G) \end{pmatrix}$$

$$= \begin{pmatrix} A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \cdot (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G)^{\mathsf{T}} \\ A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[V] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \tilde{V} \\ A_{\mathsf{mac}}[S_1] + r_M A_{\mathsf{mac}}[X_1] + r_x (A_{\mathsf{mac}}[G]) + c_{\mathsf{mac}} (r_M X_1 + r_x G) \\ A_{\mathsf{mac}}[T_1] + r_M A_{\mathsf{mac}}[X_1] + r_y (A_{\mathsf{mac}}[G]) + c_{\mathsf{mac}} (r_M Y_1 + r_y G) \end{pmatrix}$$

$$= \begin{pmatrix} A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G, V] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \cdot (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G, \tilde{V})^{\mathsf{T}} \\ A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[S_1] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \tilde{S}_1 \\ A'_{\mathsf{mac}}[T_1] + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \tilde{T}_1 \end{pmatrix}$$

$$= A'_{\mathsf{mac}} + c_{\mathsf{mac}} \cdot (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z, G, \tilde{V}, \tilde{S}_1, \tilde{T}_1)^{\mathsf{T}}$$

Note that we only used that  $(A_{\text{mac}}, c_{\text{mac}}, z_{\text{mac}})$  is a valid transcript which is useful for blindness. To conclude, observe that the user derives the transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{\text{mac}}, \widetilde{c}_{\text{mac}}, \widetilde{z}_{\text{mac}})$  from  $(A'_{\text{mac}}, c_{\text{mac}}, \beta^{-1} z_{\text{mac}}[u], z_{\text{mac}}[z, x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, \rho_0])$  via Rand from Lemma 2.18. Therefore, the transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{\text{mac}}, \widetilde{c}_{\text{mac}}, \widetilde{z}_{\text{mac}})$  remains valid for  $x_{\text{dleq}}$  as Rand satisfies Definition 2.16.

MAC BLINDING FACTORS The transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}})$  is computed by the user via  $w_{\mathsf{rnd}} = (\rho_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \alpha_0, \alpha_1, \gamma_{\mathsf{os}}, r_x, r_y, r_M, A_{\mathsf{os}})$  for  $x_{\mathsf{rnd}} \leftarrow (W, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)$ . That is, the user sets  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{rnd}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Init}(\mathsf{pp}, x_{\mathsf{rnd}})$ , derives  $\mathsf{BlindChal}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  from  $\mathsf{H}$  and sets  $\widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}} \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Resp}(\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}})$ . It is straightforward to verify that  $(x_{\mathsf{rnd}}, x_{\mathsf{rnd}}) \in \mathcal{S}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . Thus,  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}})$  is a valid transcript for  $x_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  by correctness of  $\mathcal{S}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ .

# <span id="page-26-0"></span>6 OMSUF Proof of BS<sub>alg</sub>

We show that  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathrm{alg}}$  satisfies one-more strong unforgeability.

### <span id="page-26-1"></span>6.1 Proof of Theorem 3.5

Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be an adversary against the OMSUF game of  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ , running in time  $t_{\mathcal{A}}$ , making at most  $Q_{\mathsf{S}} = Q_{\mathsf{S}}(\lambda), Q_{\mathsf{H}} = Q_{\mathsf{H}}(\lambda)$ , and  $Q_{\mathsf{pb}} = Q_{\mathsf{pb}}(\lambda)$  queries to oracles  $\mathsf{S}_1$ ,  $\mathsf{H}$ , and  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$ , respectively. Due to Lemma 2.6, we assume that it makes  $Q_{\mathsf{S}}$  to oracle  $\mathsf{S}_2$  as well, i.e., completing all started sessions. Also, denote  $Q_{\mathsf{S},\mathsf{info}}$  as the number of  $\mathsf{S}_1$  queries made with common message info  $(Q_{\mathsf{S}} = \sum_{\mathsf{info}} Q_{\mathsf{S},\mathsf{info}})$ . At the end of the game,  $\mathcal{A}$  outputs its forgeries, namely  $(\mathsf{info}^*, (\mu^{(i)}, \sigma^{(i)})_{i \in [Q_{\mathsf{S},\mathsf{info}}*+1]})$ . Note that we assume that  $\mathcal{A}$  gives exactly  $\ell = Q_{\mathsf{S},\mathsf{info}}*+1$  forgeries instead of  $\ell > Q_{\mathsf{S},\mathsf{info}}*$  for simplicity, and will use  $\ell$  throughout the proof to refer to this value. For simplicity of the notations, we assume that the query count to the random oracles  $\mathsf{H}$  and  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$  includes the query made by the game in the signing oracle and forgery verification. (This means that  $Q_{\mathsf{H}}$  and  $Q_{\mathsf{pb}}$  is at most  $Q_{\mathsf{S}}+1$  more than the number of queries actually made by  $\mathcal{A}$ .) For simplicity, we also assume that  $\mathcal{A}$  does not make the same random oracle (RO) query twice.

Now, we establish the notations for messages sent throughout the game. For the j-th signing session (determined by the j-th query to  $S_1$  with  $j \in [Q_S]$ ), we use subscript j to denote the messages being sent in this signing session (i.e., for any value x sent in the j-th session, we write  $x_j$ ). Also, we parse the i-th  $(i \in [\ell])$  forgery of A along with the corresponding statements as

$$\begin{split} \sigma^{(i)} &= (\widetilde{M}^{(i)}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)} = (\widetilde{U}^{(i)}, \widetilde{V}^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_0^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_0^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_1^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_1^{(i)}), \\ \mathrm{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}}^{(i)})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}}) \;, \\ \mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)} &= (\mathsf{ipp}, \widetilde{M}^{(i)}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)}) \;, & \mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)} &= (W, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{M}^{(i)}, \widetilde{U}^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_1^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_1^{(i)}) \;, \end{split}$$

with  $x_{os} = W, x_{dleq} = (D_1, H(info^*))$ . Then, we consider the following sequence of games, where we denote  $Pr[G^A \Rightarrow 1]$  (omitting the parameter  $\lambda$ ) as the probability of A winning in game G.

{27}------------------------------------------------

Game G<sub>0</sub> (Original OMSUF Game): This game samples the secret key sk as in the scheme and runs the signing oracles honestly. The adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  wins if all forgeries (info\*,  $(\mu^{(i)}, \sigma^{(i)})_{i \in [\ell]}$ ) verify and  $(\mu^{(i)}, \sigma^{(i)})$  are all distinct. Note that

$$\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathrm{omsuf}}_{\mathsf{BS}_{\mathrm{alg}}}(\mathcal{A},\lambda) = \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_0^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$$
.

Game  $G_1$  (No forgery with the same H query): In this game, after A outputs the forgeries, the game aborts if there exist  $i_0 \neq i_1$  with  $i_0, i_1 \in [\ell]$  such that for the corresponding hash queries

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{HQry}^{(i_0)} := & \ (\widetilde{M}^{(i_0)}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i_0)}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i_0)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_0)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i_0)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}^{(i_0)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i_0)}, \mu^{(i_0)}, \mathsf{info}^*) \ , \\ \mathsf{HQry}^{(i_1)} := & \ (\widetilde{M}^{(i_1)}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i_1)}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i_1)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_1)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i_1)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}^{(i_1)}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i_1)}, \mu^{(i_1)}, \mathsf{info}^*) \ , \end{split}$$

we have that  $\mathsf{HQry}^{(i_0)} = \mathsf{HQry}^{(i_1)}$ . Denote the event SameQuery as  $\mathcal{A}$  winning in  $\mathbf{G}_0$  but not in  $\mathbf{G}_1$ . We can see that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_0^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_1^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] + \Pr[\mathsf{SameQuery}].$$

Then, the following lemma gives a bound on the probability of SameQuery by relying on relaxed unique responses of the  $\Sigma$ -protocols.

<span id="page-27-0"></span>**Lemma 6.1.** There exist adversaries  $\mathcal{B}_{ur,os}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}_{ur,mac}$  and  $\mathcal{B}_{ur,rnd}$  such that

$$\mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{SameQuery}] \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{sbind}}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur},\mathsf{rnd}},\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{dl}}_{\mathsf{GGen}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur},\mathsf{os}},\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{sbind}}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur},\mathsf{mac}},\lambda) + \frac{Q_{\mathsf{pb}}+1}{n} \; .$$

Moreover, all these adversaries runs in time  $T_{\text{ur,os}}, T_{\text{ur,mac}}, T_{\text{ur,rnd}} \approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$ .

Proof (of Lemma 6.1). By definition of SameQuery, we have that all forgeries are valid, meaning the  $\Sigma_{\text{xxx}}$  transcripts  $(\widetilde{A}_{\text{xxx}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{c}_{\text{xxx}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{c}_{\text{xxx}}^{(i)})$  for  $\text{xxx} \in \{\text{os, mac, dleq, rnd}\}$  are valid with respect to their corresponding statement. We now consider the two forgeries indexed  $i_0, i_1$  in the event. Recall that the two forgeries correspond to the same H query  $\text{HQry}^{(i_0)} = \text{HQry}^{(i_1)}$  which contains  $\widetilde{M}^{(i_0)} = \widetilde{M}^{(i_1)}$ , the blinded tag  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\text{mac}}^{(i_0)} = \widetilde{\sigma}_{\text{mac}}^{(i_1)}$ , the commitment  $\text{cmt}_{\text{rnd}}^{(i_0)} = \text{cmt}_{\text{rnd}}^{(i_1)}$ , identical nonces  $\widetilde{A}_{\text{xxx}}^{(i_0)} = \widetilde{A}_{\text{xxx}}^{(i_1)}$  for all xxx and message  $\mu^{(i_0)} = \mu^{(i_1)}$ . However, the two forgeries are distinct by the winning condition. Therefore, the differences can only come from the challenges  $\widetilde{c}_{\text{xxx}}$  or responses  $\widetilde{z}_{\text{xxx}}$  parts of the forgery, which are the only non-identical parts.

We now consider the following cases on how the two forgeries can differ:

**Distinct challenges:** Note that because  $\tilde{c}_{os}$  and  $\tilde{c}_{rnd}$  are outputs of H and the queries are the same, they cannot differ. Thus, it could only be the case that  $\tilde{c}_{mac}^{(i_0)} \neq \tilde{c}_{mac}^{(i_1)}$  or  $\tilde{c}_{dleq}^{(i_0)} \neq \tilde{c}_{dleq}^{(i_1)}$ . However, these two cases are identical because by verification of  $\mathsf{BS}_{alg}.\mathsf{Ver}$ ,  $\tilde{c}_{mac}^{(i_0)} + \tilde{c}_{dleq}^{(i_0)} = \tilde{c}_{mac}^{(i_1)} + \tilde{c}_{dleq}^{(i_1)}$  since they are the output of the same H query. Hence, we only focus on the case that  $\tilde{c}_{dleq}^{(i_0)} \neq \tilde{c}_{dleq}^{(i_1)}$ .

In this case, since two  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  transcripts  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{dleq}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{dleq}}^{(i)})_{i \in \{i_0, i_1\}}$  are valid for the same statement defined by  $(D_2^*, D_3^*) = \mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}(\mathsf{info}^*)$ , by 2-special-soundness and the fact that the nonces are identical, we have that  $\mathsf{dlog}_G D_2^* = \mathsf{dlog}_{D_1} D_3^*$ . However, recall that outputs to  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$  are uniformly random in  $\mathbb{G}^2$ , so this case only occurs with probability at most  $Q_{\mathsf{pb}}/p$ .

Identical challenges, but distinct responses: Here, we consider different cases based on which  $\Sigma_{xxx}$  whose responses  $\widetilde{z}_{xxx}^{(i_0)} \neq \widetilde{z}_{xxx}^{(i_1)}$  are distinct. In particular, we will invoke the relaxed unique-response extractor  $\Sigma_{xxx}$ . URExt of these  $\Sigma$ -protocols. For simplicity, we will refer to the identical queries as  $(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}, \operatorname{cmt}_{rnd}, \widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{A}_{mac}, \widetilde{A}_{dleq}, \widetilde{A}_{rnd}, \mu, \operatorname{info}^*)$ , the challenges as  $\widetilde{c}_{xxx}$ , and the corresponding statements for each of these as  $x_{xxx}$ .

1.  $\Sigma_{os}$ : In this case, computing  $w = \delta_{os} \leftarrow \Sigma_{os}.\mathsf{URExt}(x_{os}, (A_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{os}, \widetilde{z}_{os}^{(i)})_{i \in \{i_0, i_1\}})$  gives us  $\delta_{os,0}G + \delta_{os,1}H = 0_{\mathbb{G}}$  and  $\delta_{os} \neq \mathbf{0}$ , by definition of  $\widetilde{\mathfrak{R}}_{os}$  that  $\phi^{os}(w) = 0_{\mathbb{G}}$ . Thus,  $\mathsf{dlog}_G H = -\delta_{os,0} \cdot \delta_{os,1}^{-1}$  can be efficiently computed; so we can construct a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur},os}$  simulating the game to  $\mathcal{A}$  (as  $\mathsf{dlog}_G H$  is not needed in  $\mathbf{G}_0$ ) and upper bounding the probability of this case occurring.

{28}------------------------------------------------

2.  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$ : We can extract  $w \leftarrow \Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathsf{URExt}(\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac}}, (A_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)})_{i \in \{i_0, i_1\}})$  where  $((\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac}}), w') \in \widetilde{\mathfrak{R}}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Notably  $w = (\delta_u, \delta_{x,0}, \delta_{x,1}, \delta_{y,0}, \delta_{y,1}, \delta_z, \delta_\rho) \neq (\mathbf{0} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^6, 0 \in \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathcal{R})$  such that  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}(w) = 0$ , which includes the following equations

$$\delta_u \widetilde{U} = 0_{\mathbb{G}} , \qquad (\delta_{x,1}, \delta_{y,1}, \delta_z) F = (0_{\mathbb{G}}, 0_{\mathbb{G}}, 0_{\mathbb{G}}) ,$$

$$\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{mck}, (\delta_{x,0}, \delta_{y,0}); \delta_{\varrho}) = \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{mck}, (0,0); 0) .$$

We know  $\widetilde{U} \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}$ , so  $\delta_u = 0$ . Unless  $F = 0_{\mathbb{G}}$  (occurs with probability 1/p), we also have  $(\delta_{x,1}, \delta_{y,1}, \delta_z) = \mathbf{0}$ . This means that  $(\delta_{x,0}, \delta_{y,0}) \neq 0$  or  $\delta_{\rho} \neq 0$ . This however violates the strong binding property of  $C_{\text{mac}}$ : we obtain a zero and non-zero opening for the same commitment. Thus, we can construct a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\text{ur,mac}}$  simulating the game to  $\mathcal{A}$  (recall  $\mathbf{G}_0$  samples pp with  $\mathsf{BS}_{\text{alg}}$ . Setup which coincides with how mck is sampled) upper bounding the probability of this case occurring.

- 3.  $\Sigma_{\text{dleq}}$ : Since  $\Sigma_{\text{dleq}}$  satisfies unique responses, this case cannot occur.
- 4.  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ : We can extract  $\mathbb{W} \leftarrow \Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{URExt}(\mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)})_{i \in \{i_0, i_1\}})$  where  $((\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{rnd}}), \mathbb{W}') \in \widetilde{\mathfrak{R}}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . Notably,  $\mathbb{W} = (\delta_{\rho}, \boldsymbol{\delta} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^6) \neq (0 \in \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathcal{R}, \mathbf{0})$  and  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{rnd}}}^{\mathsf{rnd}}(\mathbb{W}) = 0$ , which implies  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{bck}, \mathbf{0}_{\mathbb{G}}; 0) = \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{bck}, \boldsymbol{\Delta}; \delta_{\rho})$  where  $\boldsymbol{\Delta} = (\boldsymbol{\delta} \cdot \widetilde{U}, \delta_2 W \delta_0 G \delta_1 H)$ . Since  $\widetilde{U} \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}$  via the verification, if  $\boldsymbol{\delta} \neq \mathbf{0}$  then  $\boldsymbol{\Delta} \neq \mathbf{0}_{\mathbb{G}}$ . Otherwise,  $\delta_{\rho} \neq 0$ ; either of which violate strong binding of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . Therefore, we can similarly construct a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ur},\mathsf{rnd}}$  upper bounding the probability of this case occurring.  $\square$

Game  $G_2$  (Guess hash index of info\*): In this game, a uniformly random index  $i_{pb}^* \leftarrow [Q_{pb}]$  is sampled at the beginning of the game, and when A outputs the forgeries, the game aborts if  $\inf_{i_{pb}^*} \neq \inf_{i_{pb}^*}$ . From this point on, we will also interchangeably call signing sessions for signing  $\inf_{i_{pb}^*}$  as signing  $\inf_{i_{pb}^*}$ .

Since  $Q_{pb}$  includes the queries to  $H_{pb}$  made by the game, there exists  $i_{pb} \in [Q_{pb}]$  such that  $\inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * = \inf_{i_{pb}} * =$ 

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_1^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant Q_{\mathsf{pb}} \cdot \Pr[\mathbf{G}_2^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$$
.

Game  $G_3$  (Generate bck with extraction trapdoor): In this game, the commitment key bck is generated along with a trapdoor td. That is, the game sets  $(bck, td) \leftarrow C_{rnd}$ . ExtSetup $(1^{\lambda})$  for the extractor Ext =  $(C_{rnd}$ . ExtSetup,  $C_{rnd}$ . Extract) of  $C_{rnd}$  (via extraction property of  $C_{rnd}$ ).

By extractability of  $C_{rnd}$ , we can then construct an adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{dist}$  running in time  $T_{dist} \approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$\left| \Pr[\mathbf{G}_2^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \Pr[\mathbf{G}_3^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \right| \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}},\mathsf{Ext}}^{\mathsf{ext-dist}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dist}}, \lambda) \; .$$

Game  $G_4$  (Extract from  $\operatorname{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)}$  in the forgeries): When  $\mathcal{A}$  returns the forgeries containing info\* and  $(\mu^{(i)}, \sigma^{(i)})_{i \in [Q_{\mathsf{S,info}}^*]}$ ), this game efficiently extract for each  $i \in [\ell]$  the following group elements

$$(\overline{A}_0^{(i)}, \overline{A}_1^{(i)}, \overline{\Gamma}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)}, \overline{R}_x^{(i)}, \overline{R}_y^{(i)}, \overline{R}_M^{(i)}, \overline{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{td}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)}) \; .$$

Since these extracted elements are not used to determine the winning condition, we have that

$$\mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_3^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$$
.

We note that by extractability of  $C_{rnd}$  when bck is generated with an extraction trapdoor, these extracted elements are the only possible elements with valid openings for  $\operatorname{cmt}_{rnd}^{(i)}$ . Now, we consider the two following events with respect to the extracted  $(\overline{A}_{os}^{(i)})_{i \in [\ell]}$ .

• NonceColl: The adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in  $\mathbf{G}_4$ , and there exist  $i_0 \neq i_1$  with  $i_0, i_1 \in [\ell]$  such that

$$\overline{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_0)} = \overline{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_1)}.$$

• NonceDist: The adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in  $\mathbf{G}_4$ , and for all  $i_0, i_1 \in [\ell]$  with  $i_0 \neq i_1$ , we have

$$\overline{A}_{os}^{(i_0)} \neq \overline{A}_{os}^{(i_1)}.$$

{29}------------------------------------------------

Observe that these two events are efficiently checkable, and this will be relevant later on in some game hops in Section 6.3. It is easy to see that the two events are disjoint, and NonceColl  $\vee$  NonceDist is equivalent to  $\mathcal{A}$  winning in the game  $\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}}$ , we have

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr_{\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}}}[\mathsf{NonceColl}] + \Pr_{\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}}}[\mathsf{NonceDist}].$$

Thus, to conclude the proof, we bound the two probabilities as established in the following lemmas.

The case NonceColl is analyzed via a reduction to DL with the core technical idea being that an Okamoto-Schnorr witness (different from the one used to simulate the game) is likely to be extracted from the two forgeries with colliding  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i_0)} = \overline{A}_{os}^{(i_1)}$ .

The case NonceDist follows from a reduction to UF-RMA security of  $M_{alg}$ . Note that the nonces  $A_{os}$  from singing sessions of  $info^*$  are exactly the values for which a valid tag is issued, and due to Lemma 2.6 (all signing sessions are completed), there must be an extracted nonce  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i)}$  that has not yet been tagged during signing of  $info^*$ . For signing on  $info \neq info^*$ , we will later move to a game where the MAC tags are not generated honestly. To avoid issues with rewinding, we will sample all nonces  $A_{os}$  in advance to avoid tagging new nonces during the second run. Finally, the bound in the theorem statement follows via inspection.  $\Box$ 

<span id="page-29-1"></span>**Lemma 6.2.** There exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$  running in time  $T_{dlog} \approx 3 \cdot T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$\mathsf{Pr}_{\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}}} \big[ \mathsf{NonceColl} \big] \leqslant \frac{Q_\mathsf{H}^2 + 9Q_\mathsf{H}}{p} + 2\sqrt[3]{32Q_\mathsf{H}^2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_\mathsf{GGen}^\mathsf{dl}(\mathcal{B}_\mathsf{dl}, \lambda)} \; .$$

<span id="page-29-2"></span>**Lemma 6.3.** There exist adversaries  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  running in time  $T_{alg} \approx 2 \cdot T_{\mathcal{A}}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}_{hide}$  running in time  $T_{hide} \approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$ , and  $\mathcal{B}_{ddh,k}$  (for  $k \in [4]$ ) running in time  $T_{ddh,k} \approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathbf{G}_{4}^{\mathcal{A}}} \big[ \mathsf{NonceDist} \big] &\leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen},Q_{\mathsf{pb}}}^{\mathsf{qddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},1},\lambda) + 2\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen},Q_{\mathsf{S}}}^{\mathsf{qddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},2},\lambda) \\ &+ 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{hide}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{hide}},\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},3},\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},4},\lambda) \\ &+ \sqrt{Q_{\mathsf{H}} \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}}^{\mathsf{ufrma}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{alg}},\lambda)} + \frac{3Q_{\mathsf{H}} + 3Q_{\mathsf{S}} + 3}{p} \; . \end{split}$$

Moreover,  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  makes at most  $Q_S$  queries to its  $Tag(\cdot)$  oracle.

### <span id="page-29-0"></span>6.2 Proof of Lemma 6.2 (Extracting DLOG from Nonce Collision)

We refer the readers to the proof sketch of this case in Section 3.3. In this proof, we consider the same adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  as in Section 6.1 within the game  $\mathbf{G}_4$  with the winning condition changed to NonceColl occurring. We let indices  $i_0, i_1 \in [\ell]$  with  $i_0 < i_1$  denote the lexicographically smallest pair  $(i_0, i_1)$  that satisfy conditions for NonceColl. We stick to the same notations as in Section 6.1 and consider the following sequence of games  $\mathbf{G}_{A.k}$  for  $k \in [0, 4]$ .

Game  $G_{A.0}$  ( $G_4$  with NonceColl as winning condition): This game is identical to  $G_4$  except that the adversary now only wins if NonceColl occurs. We can see that

$$\mathsf{Pr}_{\mathbf{G}_{4}^{\mathcal{A}}} \big[ \mathsf{NonceColl} \big] = \mathsf{Pr} \big[ \mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.0}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \big] \; .$$

Game  $G_{A.1}$  (Extract from cmt<sub>rnd</sub> in all H queries): When A makes H queries of the form

$$(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \operatorname{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mu, \mathsf{info})$$
,

the game also extracts from cmt<sub>rnd</sub> the group elements

$$(\overline{A}_0, \overline{A}_1, \overline{\Gamma}_{os}, \overline{R}_x, \overline{R}_y, \overline{R}_M, \overline{A}_{os}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{td}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}) \;,$$

{30}------------------------------------------------

as done with the forgeries. Since this change affects neither the simulation nor the winning condition, we have

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{A \ 0}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{A \ 1}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

The changes from this point on will be inefficient checks on the forgeries. Note that the final reduction will still be efficient as it does not explicitly implement these checks. However, the goal for introducing them is to bound the probability that the forgeries fix the underlying nonces and blinding factors which can be used to break DL; and consequently, this probability will be relevant in the analysis of the reduction.

Game  $G_{A.2}$  (Abort if "extracted unblinded challenges" are equal): At the end of the game, this game introduces an additional abort: for each  $i \in [\ell]$ , let  $\gamma_{os}^{(i)} = \text{dlog}_{\widetilde{U}^{(i)}} \overline{\varGamma}_{os}^{(i)}$  and  $\alpha_{os}^{(i)} = \text{dlog}_{\widetilde{U}^{(i)}} (\overline{A}_0^{(i)}, \overline{A}_1^{(i)})$ , then it aborts if

<span id="page-30-1"></span><span id="page-30-0"></span>
$$\gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i_0)} - \tilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i_0)} = \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i_1)} - \tilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i_1)} . \tag{6}$$

Intuitively, this bad event implies that unblinded challenges of  $\widetilde{c}_{os}^{(i_0)}$  and  $\widetilde{c}_{os}^{(i_1)}$  are identical, which would not allow our final reduction to extract the underlying witness of the Okamoto-Schnorr public key W.

We now argue that the introduced above occurs with small probability. We consider each pair of queries  $\mathsf{HQry}$  and  $\mathsf{HQry}'$  to  $\mathsf{H}$ , with  $\mathsf{HQry}'$  being the later query and will later apply the union bound over the  $\binom{Q_\mathsf{H}}{2} \leqslant Q_\mathsf{H}^2$  queries. For these two queries, denote

$$\mathsf{HQry} := (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1), \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mu, \mathsf{info}) , \tag{7}$$

$$\mathsf{HQry}' := (\widetilde{M}', \widetilde{\sigma}'_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\widetilde{U}', \widetilde{V}', \widetilde{S}'_0, \widetilde{T}'_0, \widetilde{S}'_1, \widetilde{T}'_1), \operatorname{cmt}'_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{A}'_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{A}'_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{A}'_{\mathsf{dleg}}, \widetilde{A}'_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mu', \mathsf{info}') , \tag{8}$$

the corresponding bad event which leads to the abort is such that

$$\mathsf{dlog}_{\widetilde{U}}\overline{\varGamma}_{\mathsf{os}} - \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}} = \mathsf{dlog}_{\widetilde{U}'}\overline{\varGamma}'_{\mathsf{os}} - \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{os}} ,$$

where  $\tilde{c}_{os}$  and  $\tilde{c}'_{os}$  are parts of the output of H(HQry) and H(HQry'), respectively. At the time that  $\mathcal{A}$  made the query HQry', HQry and  $\tilde{c}_{os}$  are already fixed; and hence,  $\overline{\varGamma}_{os}, \tilde{c}_{os}, \overline{\varGamma}'_{os}$  as well. Thus, the probability that Equation (6) occurs is at most 1/p due to  $\tilde{c}'_{os}$  being uniformly random in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ . Accordingly, we have that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.1}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.2}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] + \frac{Q_{\mathrm{H}}^{2}}{p} \; .$$

Game  $G_{A.3}$  (Abort if the extracted  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i)}$  is not unblinded  $\widetilde{A}_{os}^{(i)}$ ): At the end of the game, the game introduces the following abort: if there exists an  $i \in [\ell]$  such that for  $\alpha_{os}^{(i)}, \gamma_{os}^{(i)}$  as defined in the previous game

$$\overline{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \neq \widetilde{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} - \phi_{\text{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{\text{os}}}^{\text{os}}(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) + \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \cdot W$$
.

Observe here that the commitment key bck is generated with extraction trapdoor and via extractability of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . Therefore, if such an event occurs, the corresponding statement  $\mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)} = (W, X_1, Y_1, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)}, \widetilde{M}^{(i)}, \widetilde{U}^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_1^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_1)^{(i)}$  is not in the language induced by the map  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp},\mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)}}^{\mathsf{rnd}}$ .

We now bound the probability that such abort can occur via special-soundness of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . We consider each RO query HQry to H parse as in Equation (7). Via 2-special-soundness of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ , we have that if the corresponding statement  $\mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{rnd}} = (W, X_1, Y_1, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)$  parsed from HQry is not in the language, there is at most one challenge  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  which allows the adversary to output a valid response  $\widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  to the nonce  $\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . Hence, there is at most 1/p probability of such uniformly random  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  being sampled; thus, by the union bound over H queries, we have

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.2}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.3}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] + \frac{Q_{\mathsf{H}}}{p}$$
.

{31}------------------------------------------------

We note that this game ensures that for all  $i \in [\ell]$ , we have

$$\begin{split} \overline{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} &= \widetilde{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} - \phi_{\text{pp}, \mathbf{x}_{\text{os}}}^{\text{os}}(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) + \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \cdot W \\ &= \phi_{\text{pp}, \mathbf{x}_{\text{os}}}^{\text{os}}(\widetilde{z}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} - \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) - (\widetilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} - \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) \cdot W \;. \end{split}$$

Game  $G_{A.4}$  (Abort if the to-be-extracted witness of W is not new): At the end of the game, the game introduces an abort with respect to the  $i_0$ -th and  $i_1$ -th forgeries as defined in the event NonceColl (i.e.,  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i_0)} = \overline{A}_{os}^{(i_1)}$ ). In particular, the game aborts if

$$(\gamma_{os}^{(i_0)} - \gamma_{os}^{(i_1)} + \widetilde{c}_{os}^{(i_1)} - \widetilde{c}_{os}^{(i_0)}) \cdot \boldsymbol{w} \neq \widetilde{z}_{os}^{(i_0)} - \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{os}^{(i_0)} - \widetilde{z}_{os}^{(i_1)} + \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{os}^{(i_1)}$$
.

We remark again that these checks are not efficient; our reduction will not implement these checks. However, we will define a good event later on which will happen with prob of adv winning in  $G_4$ . Then, we will relate this particular event occurring to the event that the reduction successfully breaks DL. The following claim then lower bounds  $\mathcal{A}$ 's winning probability in  $G_{A.4}$ .

<span id="page-31-2"></span>Lemma 6.4. 
$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{A.3}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant 2 \cdot \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{A.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

*Proof.* We prove this claim in two steps:

- 1. First, we show that for any (not necessarily efficient) adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  given group element W (generated by sampling  $\mathbf{w} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  and setting  $W = \phi_{\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{os}}^{\mathsf{os}}(\mathbf{w})$ ) and oracle access to the Okamoto-Schnorr signing protocol (as in Figure 9), its probability of finding any preimage  $\mathbf{w}'$  of W with respect to the map  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{os}}^{\mathsf{os}}$  is at most twice the probability of finding a different preimage  $\mathbf{w}' \neq \mathbf{w}$ . The former corresponds to the game PR and the latter to CR.
- 2. Second, we relate the above cases to games  $G_{A.3}$  and  $G_{A.4}$ . In particular, we will show that the winning event in game  $G_{A.3}$  corresponds to finding a preimage of W, and the winning event in game  $G_{A.4}$  corresponds to finding a different preimage of W.

<span id="page-31-0"></span>**Lemma 6.5 (Preimage to collision-finding).** Consider the games in Figure 9. For any adversary (possibly unbounded)  $\mathcal{A}$ ,  $\Pr[\operatorname{PR}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda) \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant 2 \cdot \Pr[\operatorname{CR}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda) \Rightarrow 1]$ .

Proof (of Lemma 6.5). The proof is mostly identical that of [TZ23, Theorem 1.], but we include it since their theorem statement does not directly imply our lemma statement. In particular, their statement shows an existence of another adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  breaking collision resistance using  $\mathcal{A}$ , but in our case, we need to bound probability that  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in PR with the probability that  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in CR of the same adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ .

Observe that the execution of this game depends on  $pp_{os} = (\mathbb{G}, p, G, H)$ , the random coins  $\rho_{\mathcal{A}}$  of  $\mathcal{A}$ , and the random values  $\boldsymbol{w}, \boldsymbol{r}_1, \dots, \boldsymbol{r}_{Q_{\mathbb{S}}} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^2$ . We denote the two following sets WIN<sub>PR</sub> and WIN<sub>CR</sub> as the sets of inp =  $(pp = (pp_{os}, \rho_{\mathcal{A}}), \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r} = (\boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [Q_{\mathbb{S}}]})$  that makes  $\mathcal{A}$  wins the games  $PR_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$  (finding a preimage of W) and  $CR_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$  (finding a preimage  $\boldsymbol{w}' \neq \boldsymbol{w}$  of W), respectively.

We now consider a map  $\Psi(\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r})$  which preserves the view of  $\mathcal{A}$ , similar to the proofs of [TZ23, Theorem 1] and [HKL19, Lemma 7.3]. First, we let  $\boldsymbol{c}(\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r}) = (c_i)_{i \in [Q_S]}$  denote the values  $c_{\mathrm{sid}}$  that  $\mathcal{A}(\mathsf{pp}_{\mathrm{os}}, W = w_0 G + w_1 H); \rho_{\mathcal{A}})$  queries  $S_2$  with. Then, let  $\Psi : (\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r}) \mapsto (\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w} + \boldsymbol{\Delta}, \mathbf{r} - \boldsymbol{c}(\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r})\boldsymbol{\Delta})$  where  $\boldsymbol{\Delta} = (-\mathsf{dlog}_G H, 1)$ . We claim that this map preserves the view of  $\mathcal{A}$ .

- pp remains the same.
- W is unchanged. This is because  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{os}}}^{\mathsf{os}}(\boldsymbol{\Delta}) = 0_{\mathbb{G}}$ , so by linearity  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{os}}}^{\mathsf{os}}(\boldsymbol{w}) = \phi_{\mathsf{pp}_{\mathsf{os}}}^{\mathsf{os}}(\boldsymbol{w} + \boldsymbol{\Delta})$ .
- The outputs of  $S_1$  remains unchanged with the similar linearity argument above.
- Finally, we can inductively argue that the output of  $S_2$  is unchanged as follows: note that for any r and c,  $r + cw = r c\Delta + c \cdot (w + \Delta)$ ; thus, it is only left to argue that  $c(pp, w, r) = c(\Psi(pp, w, r))$ . Assume that the queries made to  $S_2$  are identical up to the i-th  $(i \in [Q_S])$  query between the two runs (with (pp, w, r)) and  $\Psi(pp, w, r)$ ), then by the above observation, the output of this query is also identical. Therefore, the view of A remains the same.

<span id="page-31-1"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>6</sup> We removed  $x_{os}$  from the map definition to make it clear that the map only depends on  $pp_{os}$ .

{32}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-32-0"></span>

| Gam  | e $\operatorname{PR}_{GGen}^{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$ : $\operatorname{CR}_{GGen}^{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$ :               | Orac | ele S <sub>1</sub> ():                                       |
|------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------|--------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1:   | $\mathcal{S} \leftarrow \emptyset$                                                                                      | 1:   | $Q \leftarrow Q + 1$                                         |
| 2:   | $(\mathbb{G},p,G) \leftarrow \$ GGen(1^{\lambda})$                                                                      | 2:   | $\boldsymbol{r}_Q \leftarrow \$~\mathbb{Z}_p^2$              |
| 3:   | $H \leftarrow \mathbb{S} \; \mathbb{G} \; ; \boldsymbol{w} \leftarrow \mathbb{S} \; \mathbb{Z}_p^2 \; ; Q \leftarrow 0$ | 3:   | $\mathbf{return}\ (Q,\phi_{pp_{os}}^{os}(\boldsymbol{r}_Q))$ |
| 4:   | $pp_{os} \leftarrow (\mathbb{G}, p, G, H)$                                                                              | Orac | ele $S_2(sid, c_{sid})$ :                                    |
| 5:   | $W \leftarrow w_0 G + w_1 H$                                                                                            | 1:   | if $sid \in \mathcal{S}$ then return $\bot$                  |
| 6.   | $\boldsymbol{w}' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathrm{S}_1,\mathrm{S}_2}(pp_os,W)$                                           | 2:   | $\mathcal{S} \leftarrow \mathcal{S} \cup \{\mathrm{sid}\}$   |
| 1 0. | (I I os)                                                                                                                |      |                                                              |

**Fig. 9.** Preimage and collision resistance games for  $\phi_{pp_{os}}^{os}$ . We left out the  $x_{os}$  since the map only depends on G and H.

Since this map preserves the view of  $\mathcal{A}$ , we can see that it is a bijection as the inverse  $\Psi': (\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r}) \mapsto (\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w} - \boldsymbol{\Delta}, \mathbf{r} + \boldsymbol{c}(\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r}) \boldsymbol{\Delta})$  is such that  $\Psi'(\Psi(\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r})) = (\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r})$  since  $\boldsymbol{c}(\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r}) = \boldsymbol{c}(\Psi(\mathsf{pp}, \boldsymbol{w}, \mathbf{r}))$ .

Then, we can infer that if  $\mathsf{inp} \in \mathsf{WIN}_{\mathsf{PR}}$  (i.e.,  $\mathcal{A}$  find a preimage of W), then either the output w' of  $\mathcal{A}$  is w' = w or  $w' \neq w$ . If the former case w' = w occurs, this implies that  $w' \neq w + \Delta$ ; thus,  $\Psi(\mathsf{inp}) \in \mathsf{WIN}_{\mathsf{CR}}$  because  $\Psi$  preserve the view of  $\mathcal{A}$ , so the output of  $\mathcal{A}$  is preserved. If the latter case occurs  $w' \neq w$ , so  $\mathsf{inp} \in \mathsf{WIN}_{\mathsf{CR}}$ .

Therefore, we have that

$$\begin{split} \text{Pr}[\mathsf{inp} \in \mathrm{WIN_{CR}}] &= \frac{1}{2} (\text{Pr}[\mathsf{inp} \in \mathrm{WIN_{CR}}] + \text{Pr}[\mathsf{inp} \in \mathrm{WIN_{CR}}]) \\ &= \frac{1}{2} (\text{Pr}[\mathsf{inp} \in \mathrm{WIN_{CR}}] + \text{Pr}[\Psi(\mathsf{inp}) \in \mathrm{WIN_{CR}}]) \\ &\geqslant \frac{1}{2} \text{Pr}[\mathsf{inp} \in \mathrm{WIN_{CR}} \ \lor \ \Psi(\mathsf{inp}) \in \mathrm{WIN_{CR}}] \geqslant \frac{1}{2} \text{Pr}[\mathsf{inp} \in \mathrm{WIN_{PR}}] \ . \end{split}$$

The first line is trivial. The second line follows from  $\Psi$  being a bijection, so  $\Psi(\mathsf{inp})$  is identically distributed to uniformly sampled inp. The second to last inequality follows from the union bound. The last inequality follows from our observation above that  $\mathsf{inp} \in \mathsf{WIN}_{\mathsf{PR}}$  implies  $\mathsf{inp} \in \mathsf{WIN}_{\mathsf{CR}}$  or  $\Psi(\mathsf{inp}) \in \mathsf{WIN}_{\mathsf{CR}}$ . This then concludes the proof of the lemma.

RELATING THE LEMMA TO  $G_{A.3}$  AND  $G_{A.4}$ . We recall the winning conditions of the two games. In  $G_{A.3}$ , the winning condition is that (1) NonceColl occurs, (2) for the two corresponding forgeries  $i_0, i_1, \gamma_{os}^{(i_0)} - \widetilde{c}_{os}^{(i_0)} = \gamma_{os}^{(i_1)} - \widetilde{c}_{os}^{(i_1)}$  (Equation (6)), and (3) for all forgeries  $i \in [\ell]$ ,  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i)} = \phi_{pp,x_{os}}^{os}(\widetilde{z}_{os}^{(i)} - \alpha_{os}^{(i)}) - (\widetilde{c}_{os}^{(i)} - \gamma_{os}^{(i)}) \cdot W$ . Thus, by how  $i_0, i_1$  are defined, we have that

$$\begin{split} 0_{\mathbb{G}} = & \overline{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})} - \overline{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})} \\ 0_{\mathbb{G}} = & \phi_{\text{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{\text{os}}}^{\text{os}} (\widetilde{z}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})} - \pmb{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})}) - (\widetilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})} - \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})}) \cdot W - (\phi_{\text{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{\text{os}}}^{\text{os}} (\widetilde{z}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})} - \pmb{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})}) - \\ & (\widetilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})} - \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})}) \cdot W) \\ W = & \phi_{\text{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{\text{os}}}^{\text{os}} ((\widetilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})} - \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})} + \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})} - \widetilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})})^{-1} \cdot (\widetilde{z}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})} - \pmb{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{1})} - \widetilde{z}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})} + \pmb{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i_{0})})) \;. \end{split}$$

The last equality follows from the observation that the inverted  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ -element is non-zero. In this case, we see that the event implies the existence of a preimage of W, namely  $\mathbf{w}' = (\gamma_{os}^{(i_0)} - \gamma_{os}^{(i_1)} + \tilde{c}_{os}^{(i_1)} - \tilde{c}_{os}^{(i_0)})^{-1} \cdot (\tilde{z}_{os}^{(i_0)} - \alpha_{os}^{(i_0)} - \tilde{z}_{os}^{(i_1)} + \alpha_{os}^{(i_1)})$ . Similarly, we have that the winning condition in game  $\mathbf{G}_{A.4}$  is exactly when  $\mathbf{w} \neq \mathbf{w}'$ . Therefore, we can construct an adversary  $\mathcal{A}_{pr-cr}$  (given in Figures 10 and 11) that plays either the PR game or the CR game, running  $\mathcal{A}$ , and using the given oracles to simulate the signing sessions, such that  $\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{A.3}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{GGen}^{\mathcal{A}_{pr-cr}}(\lambda) \Rightarrow 1]$  and  $\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{A.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{GGen}^{\mathcal{A}_{pr-cr}}(\lambda) \Rightarrow 1]$  to conclude the proof. The adversary  $\mathcal{A}_{pr-cr}$  simulates the game  $\mathbf{G}_{A.3}$  (where the oracle simulation is the same as in  $\mathbf{G}_{A.4}$ ) to  $\mathcal{A}$  except

Fig. 12. Wrapper algorithm  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  for the proof of Lemma 6.2. The oracles simulation are given in Figure 13. We denote internal states of  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$  info $[\cdot]$ , str $[\cdot]$  for mappings from indices  $i \in [Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]$  and  $i \in [Q_{\mathsf{H}}]$  to the i-th query to  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$  and  $\mathsf{H}$ , respectively; additionally,  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}[\cdot]$ ,  $\mathsf{H}[\cdot]$  are mappings from query to output of the corresponding RO. We assume that the tuple  $(\mathbb{G}, p, G)$  is implicit in  $\mathsf{pp}$ .

that the transcript of  $\Sigma_{os}$  is simulated with its oracle access in the game PR or CR. At the end of the game,  $\mathcal{A}_{pr-cr}$  extracts  $\boldsymbol{w}'$  by (inefficiently) computing the discrete logarithms of  $\overline{A}_0^{(i)}$ ,  $\overline{A}_1^{(i)}$ ,  $\overline{\Gamma}^{(i)}$  for  $i \in \{i_0, i_1\}$ . This particular step does not require rewinding as we are only analyzing specific probabilities, and so we do not run into the issues with Okamoto-Schnorr OMUF as discussed in Section 1.1.

Now we argue the claimed equalities on success probabilities. Notice that  $\mathcal{A}_{pr-cr}$  only outputs  $\boldsymbol{w}'$  if  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in game  $\mathbf{G}_{A.3}^{\mathcal{A}}$ , and that if  $\mathcal{A}$  wins,  $\phi_{pp}^{os}(\boldsymbol{w}') = W$  (i.e.,  $\mathcal{A}_{pr-cr}$  wins in PR game). Thus, the first equality is satisfied. Similarly, the additional winning condition of  $\mathbf{G}_{A.4}^{\mathcal{A}}$  is that  $\boldsymbol{w}' \neq \boldsymbol{w}$ , so the second equality follows, proving the claim.

Finally, we bound  $\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{A.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$  as in the following lemma statement. We will prove the lemma in three steps: (1) defining a wrapper algorithm to apply the forking lemma, (2) defining the reduction to DL, and (3) analyzing the reduction using the forking lemma. In particular, we will require using the forking algorithm Fork<sub>3</sub> from Lemma 2.20 to extract the blinding factors  $\alpha_{os}^{(i)}$ ,  $\gamma_{os}^{(i)}$  for  $i \in \{i_0, i_1\}$  from the  $i_0$ -th and  $i_1$ -th forgeries. Thus, this requires us to run  $\mathcal{A}$  for 3 times and fork once at the H queries corresponding to each of the forgery.

<span id="page-34-0"></span>Lemma 6.6 (Forking for NonceColl). There exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$  running in time  $T_{alg} \approx 3T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A.4}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \sqrt[3]{32Q_{\mathrm{H}}^2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dl}}, \lambda)} + \frac{4Q_{\mathrm{H}}}{p} \; .$$

We particularly note that the theorem holds, even if  $\mathcal{A}$  is computational. This is because our reduction does not perform the game's inefficient checks.

*Proof* (of Lemma 6.6). We first define the wrapper algorithm on which we will apply the forking lemma.

Fig. 13. Oracle simulation by  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  extended from Figure 12. We simplify the description of  $S_2$  be removing the sid tracking and assume that the second time an sid is queried to  $S_2$ ,  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{pr-cr}}$  simply return  $\perp$ .

WRAPPER  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$ . The wrapper  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  (defined in Figures 12 and 13) simulates the game  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{A}.4}$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ . In particular, it takes as input the public parameters  $\mathsf{pp}$  as generated in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{A}.4}$ ,  $\mathsf{ipp}$  generated along with  $\mathsf{msk}$  via  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{KeyGen}$ , extraction trapdoor  $\mathsf{td}$ , witness  $\boldsymbol{w} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  for  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{os}}$ , and prepared randomness  $((\rho_{\mathsf{S},j})_{j\in[Q_\mathsf{S}]}, (D_{2,i}, D_{3,i})_{i\in[Q_\mathsf{Pb}]}, (\tilde{c}_i)_{i\in[Q_\mathsf{H}]}, i_{\mathsf{pb}}^*)$  to be used for oracle simulation along with  $\boldsymbol{h}$ . It then runs  $\mathcal{A}$  and simulate the game as follows:

Input to A: The wrapper forwards pp and  $vk = (ipp, W = w_0G + w_1H)$  to A. Oracle simulation: We list the corresponding simulation below:

- Random oracles  $H, H_{pb}$ :  $(\tilde{c}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_p^2)_{i \in [Q_H]}$  and h are used to simulate H where the i-th query is replied with  $(\tilde{c}_i, h_i) \in \mathbb{Z}_p^3$ , while  $(D_{2,i}, D_{3,i})$  is used to simulate the i-th query to the random oracle  $H_{pb}$ .
- Signing oracles  $S_1, S_2$ : The wrapper uses  $\rho_{S,j} = (u_j, \rho_{os,j}, \rho_{\mathsf{mac},j}, \rho_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{dleq},j})$  are the randomness used to compute the transcript for the j-th signing session. In particular,  $u_j$  is the randomness for computing  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  along with  $\mathsf{msk}$ ,  $\rho_{\mathsf{os},j}$  is the randomness for  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{os}}$  transcript computed using  $\boldsymbol{w}$ ,  $\rho_{\mathsf{mac},j}$  is the randomness for  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  transcript, and  $\rho_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{dleq},j}$  are used to simulate the  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  transcript. Note that these corresponds to how the oracles are simulated in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{A}.4}$ .

Output of  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$ : The wrapper checks where the event NonceColl occurs (it uses  $i_{\mathsf{pb}}^*$  from the input as the guessed index of  $\mathsf{info}^*$ ). If so, it outputs the corresponding indices  $I_0, I_1 \in [Q_{\mathsf{H}}]$  to the H query in the verification of the  $i_0$ -th and  $i_1$ -th forgeries along with  $\sigma^{(i_0)}$ ,  $\sigma^{(i_1)}$ , respectively. Note that the two forgeries  $i_0, i_1$  exist due to how NonceColl is defined If NonceColl does not occur, it returns  $\bot$ .

We note that the wrapper does not check the additional winning condition introduced in  $\mathbf{G}_{A.2}$  to  $\mathbf{G}_{A.4}$ . This is due to these checks requiring inefficient discrete logarithm computation. However, we remark that if  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in game  $\mathbf{G}_{A.4}$ , then the output  $(I = (I_0, I_1), \sigma = (\sigma_0, \sigma_1)) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho_{\mathcal{A}})$  also satisfies the checks introduced in those games.

In particular, we consider the event Good defined over the output  $\sigma = (\sigma_0, \sigma_1)$  of  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$ . We use the same notations as in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A.4}}$  and denote  $(\cdot)^{(i_b)}$  to values corresponding to  $\sigma_b$ . We define Good to be the event that  $(\gamma_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_0)} - \gamma_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_1)} + \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_1)} - \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_0)}) \cdot \boldsymbol{w} \neq \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_0)} - \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_0)} - \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_1)} + \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i_1)}$  where  $\boldsymbol{\alpha}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)}, gamma_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)}$  are in the exponents. Note that the occurrence of Good cannot be verified efficiently, and Good is implied by  $\mathcal{A}$  winning

{36}------------------------------------------------

```
Alg. \mathcal{B}_{dl}(pp_{os} = (\mathbb{G}, p, G, H)):
   1: \mathsf{mpp} \leftarrow \mathsf{Malg}.\mathsf{Setup}(\mathbb{G}, p, G)
   2: \quad (\mathsf{bck},\mathsf{td}) \leftarrow \$ \; \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{ExtSetup}(\mathbb{G},p,G) \; ; \boldsymbol{w} \leftarrow \$ \; \mathbb{Z}_p^2
   3: pp \leftarrow (H, mpp, bck)
   4: (msk, ipp) \leftarrow M_{alg}.KeyGen(mpp)
   5: for j \in [Q_S]:
   6: \qquad u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^* \; ; \rho_{\mathsf{os},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2
   7: \rho_{\mathsf{mac},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^6 \times \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathcal{R} ; \rho_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{dleq},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p
   8: \rho_{S,j} \leftarrow (u_j, \rho_{\mathsf{mac},j}, \rho_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{mac},j})
   9: D_{2,1}, D_{3,1}, \dots, D_{2,Q_{\mathsf{pb}}}, D_{3,Q_{\mathsf{pb}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{S} \mathbb{G} ; \widetilde{c}_1, \dots, \widetilde{c}_{Q_{\mathsf{H}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{S} \mathbb{Z}_p^2 ; i_{\mathsf{pb}}^{ \bigstar} \leftarrow \mathbb{S} [Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]
10: \quad \mathsf{inp} \gets (\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{ipp}, \mathsf{msk}, \mathsf{td}, \boldsymbol{w}, (\rho_{S,j})_{j \in [Q_S]}, (D_{2,i}, D_{3,i})_{i \in [Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]}, (\tilde{c}_i)_{i \in [Q_{\mathsf{H}}]}, i_{\mathsf{pb}}^{\boldsymbol{*}})
11: \quad (\mathsf{frk}, \sigma = (\sigma_0, \sigma_1), \sigma' = (\sigma'_0, \sigma'_1)) \leftarrow \$ \ \mathsf{Fork}_3^{\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}}(\mathsf{inp})
```
