14:
                       \mathbf{parse} \ \sigma_b' = (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}', \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}}')_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}})
 15:
                       \mathbf{parse}\ \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{T}_1)
 16:
                      \mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{rnd}} = (W = w_0 G + w_1 H, X_1, Y_1, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)
 17:
                  (\alpha_0, \alpha_1, \gamma_{\mathsf{os}}, r_x, r_y, r_M, \rho_{\mathsf{rnd}}) \leftarrow \varSigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Ext}(\mathbf{x}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}', \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}')
 18:
                      z_{\text{os}}^{(b)} \leftarrow \tilde{z}_{\text{os}} - (\alpha_0, \alpha_1) \; ; \quad c_{\text{os}}^{(b)} \leftarrow \tilde{c}_{\text{os}} - \gamma_{\text{os}}
 19:
20: \quad \mathbf{if} \ c_{\mathrm{os}}^{(0)} = c_{\mathrm{os}}^{(1)} \ \mathbf{then} \ \mathbf{return} \ \bot
21: \mathbf{w}' \leftarrow (z_{\mathsf{os}}^{(1)} - z_{\mathsf{os}}^{(0)}) \cdot (c_{\mathsf{os}}^{(1)} - c_{\mathsf{os}}^{(0)})^{-1}
 22: if w = w' then return \bot
23: return (w'_0 - w_0) \cdot (w_1 - w'_1)^{-1}
```

Fig. 14. Reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$ .

in game  $G_{A.4}$ . Furthermore, for our reduction's analysis, we define an inefficient wrapper  $\mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  which runs  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  but also checks for Good on the output, and returns  $\bot$  if Good does not occur. Hence, we obtain

$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}, \rho_{\mathcal{A}}} \big[ \bot \neq (I, \sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho_{\mathcal{A}}) \big] \\ = & \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}, \rho_{\mathcal{A}}} \big[ \bot \neq (I, \sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho_{\mathcal{A}}) \ \land \ \mathsf{Good} \big] \\ \geqslant & \mathsf{Pr} \big[ \mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{A}.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \big]. \end{aligned}$$

The first equality follows from the definition of  $\mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  and the second follows from definition of  $\mathbf{G}_{A.4}$ . REWINDING REDUCTION  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dl}}$ . We now consider the reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dl}}$  (given in Figure 14) which runs  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  for three times via the forking algorithm  $\mathsf{Fork}_3$  with the input to  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}$  set up as in  $\mathbf{G}_{A.4}$  along with the required randomness for oracle simulation.

Remark 6.7. Recall that Fork<sub>3</sub> runs the wrapper once (on uniformly random  $\mathbf{h} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{Q_H}$ ), obtains two indices  $(I_0, I_1)$  along with the corresponding outputs  $(\mathsf{aux}_{I_0}, \mathsf{aux}_{I_1})$  (which are individual signatures in our cases), and runs the wrapper again twice on  $\mathbf{h}'$  and  $\mathbf{h}''$ . Here,  $\mathbf{h}'$  is uniformly sampled conditioning on the first  $I_0 - 1$  values agreeing with  $\mathbf{h}$ , and  $\mathbf{h}''$  is uniformly sampled conditioning on the first  $I_1 - 1$  values agreeing with  $\mathbf{h}$ . Then, Fork<sub>3</sub> succeeds if (1)  $h_{I_0} \neq h'_{I_0}$ , (2)  $h_{I_1} \neq h''_{I_1}$ , (3) the run using  $\mathbf{h}'$  outputs  $I_0$  as one of the index, and similarly the run using  $\mathbf{h}''$  outputs  $I_1$ . Also, Fork<sub>3</sub> outputs  $\mathsf{aux} = (\mathsf{aux}_{I_0}, \mathsf{aux}_{I_1})$  and  $\mathsf{aux}' = (\mathsf{aux}'_{I_0}, \mathsf{aux}''_{I_1})$ , where the latter is parsed from the output of the second and third runs of the wrapper, respectively.

Also, we need to rewind the adversary twice in order to extract the blinding factors from two signatures. Rewinding once does not suffice as it will only allow the reduction to extract from only one of the forgery, and we need the blinding factors from both to extract the discrete logarithm.

{37}------------------------------------------------

Within  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$ , if Fork<sub>3</sub><sup> $\mathcal{A}_{NonceColl}$ </sup> does not succeed, it aborts. Otherwise, Fork<sub>3</sub> succeeds and returns  $\sigma = (\sigma_0, \sigma_1)$  and  $\sigma' = (\sigma'_0, \sigma'_1)$ . Here,  $\sigma$  contains the  $i_0$ -th and  $i_1$ -th forgeries from the first run of  $\mathcal{A}_{NonceColl}$ . On the other hand,  $\sigma'_0$  comes from the second run of  $\mathcal{A}_{NonceColl}$  within Fork<sub>3</sub> and corresponds to the same RO query used for verifying  $\sigma_0$ . Similarly,  $\sigma'_1$  comes from the third run of  $\mathcal{A}_{NonceColl}$  and corresponds to the same RO query used for verifying  $\sigma_1$ . Then,  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$  does the following:

- 1. From both pairs  $(\sigma_b, \sigma_b')$  for  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , extract the underlying witnesses using the special-soundness extractor  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . Ext. Note that because  $\mathsf{Fork}_3$  succeeds, the two challenges for  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  transcripts are distinct.
- 2. Then, for each  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , use the extracted witness  $w_{\mathsf{rnd}} = (\alpha_0, \alpha_1, \gamma_{\mathsf{os}}, r_x, r_y, r_M, \rho_{\mathsf{rnd}})$  (omitting the superscripts (b) for readability) to compute the original Okamoto-Schnorr response and challenge

$$z_{os}^{(b)} = \widetilde{z}_{os} - (\alpha_0, \alpha_1), c_{os}^{(b)} = \widetilde{c}_{os} - \gamma_{os},$$

where  $\widetilde{z}_{os}$  and  $\widetilde{c}_{os}$  are parsed from  $\sigma_b$ .

- 3. Abort if  $c_{os}^{(0)} = c_{os}^{(1)}$ . Otherwise, compute  $\boldsymbol{w}' = (z_{os}^{(1)} z_{os}^{(0)}) \cdot (c_{os}^{(1)} c_{os}^{(0)})^{-1}$ , i.e., extracting the witness for  $\Sigma_{os}$  via special soundness.
- 4. Abort if  $\mathbf{w} = \mathbf{w}'$ . Otherwise, compute  $h = (w_0' w_0) \cdot (w_1 w_1')^{-1}$ . Note that with  $W = w_0 G + w_1 H = w_0' G + w_1' H$ , we can see that  $h = \mathsf{dlog}_G H$ .

Analysis of  $\mathcal{B}_{dl}$ . By how  $\mathcal{B}$  is constructed, we can see that if  $\mathcal{B}$  does not abort, it wins in the DL game. Accordingly, the event that  $\mathcal{B}$  does not abort corresponds to the event that in the first run of  $\mathcal{A}_{NonceColl}$  within Fork<sub>3</sub> outputs  $\sigma = (\sigma_0, \sigma_1)$  satisfying the event Good defined above; equivalently, the inefficient wrapper  $\mathcal{A}'_{NonceColl}$  does not abort. Therefore,

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{dI}}_{\mathsf{GGen}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dI}}, \lambda) \geqslant & \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp}} \big[ \mathsf{Fork}_{3}^{\mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}}(\mathsf{inp}) \neq \bot \big] \\ \geqslant & \frac{\mathsf{Pr} \big[ \mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \big]}{2} \left( \frac{\mathsf{Pr} \big[ \mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \big]}{4Q_{\mathsf{H}}} - \frac{1}{p} \right)^{2} \; , \end{split}$$

where the last inequality follows from Lemma 2.20 and that  $\mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp},\boldsymbol{h},\rho_{\mathcal{A}}}[\bot \neq (I,\sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceColl}}(\mathsf{inp},\boldsymbol{h};\rho_{\mathcal{A}})] \geqslant \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{A}.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$ . Note that  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{dl}}$  runs in time roughly  $3T_{\mathcal{A}}$ , concluding the proof.

### <span id="page-37-0"></span>6.3 Proof of Lemma 6.3 (Extracting MAC Forgeries from Distinct Nonces)

We will use the notations as in the proof of Theorem 3.5 in Section 6.1. Moreover, we number the signing sessions with indices  $j \in [Q_S]$  corresponding to the session where  $\mathcal{A}$  makes the j-th call to the oracle  $S_1$ ; accordingly, we refer to these indices as the session ID (sid in the OMSUF game)with j as well. We consider the following sequence of games  $\mathbf{G}_{B,k}$  for  $k \in [0,14]$ . To help the readers navigate the proof, we explain the high-level detail of the games in this sequence:

- Game  $G_{B.1}$  sets up the group element H while knowing the discrete logarithm. This will help later on when we give a reduction from UF-RMA security of  $M_{alg}$  where the tagging oracle knows the discrete logarithm of the message  $A_{os}$ , which is the Okamoto-Schnorr nonce.
- Games  $G_{B.2}$  to  $G_{B.7}$ : These games are used to deal with the "partially blind" part of the protocol. In particular, it simulates the signing queries on info  $\neq$  info\* by computing  $M_{alg}$  tags without using the secret key msk for these sessions, along with simulating  $\Sigma_{mac}$  side of the signing for these sessions.
- Games  $G_{B.8}$  to  $G_{B.10}$ : Enforce certain structures on the blinded  $M_{alg}$  tags  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}^{(i)}$  in the forgery to ensure that the final reduction can recover a fresh and valid  $M_{alg}$  tag.
- Games  $G_{B.11}$  to  $G_{B.12}$ : Simulate the proof of validity of the MAC ( $\Sigma_{mac}$ ), preparing for the reduction from UF-CMA security which does not know the secret key (aka witness used in  $\Sigma_{mac}$  protocol).
- Game  $G_{B.13}$  to  $G_{B.14}$ : Syntactic changes to prepare for the rewinding argument, namely sampling the randomness at the beginning of the game and preparing  $M_{alg}$  tags used in signing sessions with common message info\* in advance.

{38}------------------------------------------------

• In the final game, by definition of NonceDist, there exists some index  $i^* \in [\ell]$  (w.l.o.g. we assume  $i^*$  is the minimal such index) such that the extracted  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i^*)}$  is one of the nonces not used in the signing sessions on info\*. Thus, the blinded MAC tag will correspond to a fresh MAC forgery; accordingly, we can rewind and reduce to UF-RMA security of the MAC. Note that the reduction needs rewinding to extract (1) the blinding factor of the blinded MAC in order to recover the unblinded MAC forgery, and (2) the discrete logarithm of  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i^*)}$  which corresponds to our message for the MAC forgery. We note that due to the change in the previous game, our reduction will prepare the nonces and their MAC tags in advance, so as to avoid making extra MAC tag queries during the rewinding.

Game  $G_{B.0}$  (Game  $G_4$  with winning condition NonceDist): This game is identical to game  $G_4$  except that the winning condition is now NonceDist. We can see that

$$\mathsf{Pr}_{\mathbf{G}_{A}^{\mathcal{A}}}[\mathsf{NonceDist}] = \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B},0}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$$

Game  $G_{B.1}$  (Sample H while knowing  $h = dlog_G H$ , and compute  $w' = dlog_G W$ ,  $r'_{os,j} = dlog_G A_{os,j}$ ): This game sample  $h \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and set  $H \leftarrow hG$ . Also, set  $w' = w_0 + w_1 h = dlog_G W$  along with  $r'_{os,j} = r_{os,j,0} + r_{os,j,1}h$ , where  $r_{os,j,0}, r_{os,j,1}$  are randomness used for computing  $A_{os,j}$  in the j-th signing session. It is easy to see that this change does not affect the adversary's advantage.

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}\,0}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}\,1}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

Game  $G_{B.2}$  (Switch H(info) to be DLEQ tuples): Recall the guessed index  $i_{pb}^*$  introduced in  $G_2$ . In this game, for the *i*-th query  $info_i$  to  $H_{pb}$ , the game samples  $a_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and set  $H_{pb}(info_i) \leftarrow (a_i G, a_i D_1)$ . Note that since the winning condition (i.e., event NonceDist) is efficiently checkable, we can give a straightforward reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{ddh,1}$  from the  $Q_{pb}$ -DDH problem with running time  $T_{ddh,1} \approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$|\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}.1}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}.2}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen},Q_{\mathrm{pb}}}^{\mathsf{qddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},1},\lambda) \; .$$

Game  $G_{B.3}$  (Compute  $\Sigma_{dleq}$  honestly in signing oracles): In this game, for queries to  $S_1$  and  $S_2$  (with session ID  $j \in [Q_S]$ ) with tag info that corresponds to the *i*-th  $H_{pb}$  query with  $(D_{2,i}, D_{3,i}) \leftarrow H_{pb}(info)$ , the game computes  $(A_{dleq,j}, c_{dleq,j}, z_{dleq,j})$  as follows:

- $(1) \ \text{Compute} \ (A_{\mathsf{dleq},j},\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{dleq},j}) \leftarrow \ \, \mathcal{E}_{\mathsf{dleq}}.\mathsf{Init}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}} = (D_1, D_{2,i}, D_{3,i}), \mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{dleq}} = a_i),$
- (2) Sample  $c_{\mathsf{dleq},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$
- (3) Compute  $z_{\mathsf{dleq},j} \leftarrow \Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}.\mathsf{Resp}(\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{dleq},j})$

Due to perfect SHVZK of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$ , we have

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B},2}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B},3}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

Note also that in this game for session j's where the changes were made, the joint distribution of  $(c_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{mac},j})$  is identical to sampling  $c_{\mathsf{mac},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  first and computing  $c_{\mathsf{dleq},j} \leftarrow c_{\mathsf{or},j} - c_{\mathsf{mac},j}$ .

Game  $G_{B.4}$  (Simulate  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  in signing oracles): In this game, for queries to  $S_1$  and  $S_2$  (with session ID  $j \in [Q_S]$ ) with tag info that corresponds to the i-th  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$  query, the game computes  $(A_{\mathsf{mac},j}, c_{\mathsf{mac},j}, z_{\mathsf{mac},j})$  by: (1) sampling  $c_{\mathsf{mac},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ , (2)  $(A_{\mathsf{mac},j}, z_{\mathsf{mac},j}) \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$   $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac},j} = (\mathsf{ipp}, A_{\mathsf{os},j}, U_j, V_j, S_j, T_j, U_j, V_j, S_j, T_j, U_j, V_j, S_j, T_j, U_j, V_j, S_j, U_j, V_j, S_j, U_j, V_j, V_j, V_j, V_j, V_j, V_j, V_j, V$ 

$$\mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B},3}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B},4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$$
.

Game  $G_{B.5}$  (Computed  $M_{alg}$  tags without using msk when signing info  $\neq$  info\*): In this game, for queries to  $S_1$  (with session ID  $j \in [Q_S]$ ) with tag info that does not correspond to the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $H_{pb}$  query, the game computes the  $M_{alg}$  tag  $\sigma_{mac,j}$  as

$$u_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_n^*, U_i \leftarrow u_i F, V_i \leftarrow u_i Z, S_i, T_i \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$$
.

{39}------------------------------------------------

The advantage change follows from the following claim. The key idea of the proof is that we can view the  $U_j, x_0U_j, y_0U_j$  portions of the MAC tags as a DDH instance with respect to the bases  $(G, x_0G, y_0G)$ . Note that we do not require  $V_j$  to be uniformly random, since it can now be computed while only knowing ipp which contains Z.

The changes in this game is to prepare for the final reduction, which will only output honestly computed tags for signing sessions on  $info^*$ . Otherwise, notice that the MAC tags are, however, not bound to the common message info. If the tags given during signing of  $info \neq info^*$  were valid, the adversary could potentially use these tags in the one-more forgery. Thus, making the reduction not successful.

Remark 6.8. We only make these changes for signing queries with info  $\neq$  info\*, because later on, we still need to switch  $\mathsf{H}(\mathsf{info}^*)$  to be uniformly random to argue certain structures on the blinded MAC tags in the forgery via soundness of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  and  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$ . For these steps, we still need the MAC tags in signing queries on  $\mathsf{info}^*$  to be honestly generated to compute  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  transcript honestly and simulate  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  during signing of  $\mathsf{info}^*$ .

<span id="page-39-0"></span>Lemma 6.9 (Uniformly random  $M_{\text{alg}}$  tags). There exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{\text{ddh},2}$  playing the QDDH game running in time  $T_{\text{ddh},2} \approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  and  $\mathcal{B}_{\text{hide}}$  also running in time  $T_{\text{hide}} \approx T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.4}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.5}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen},Q_{\mathrm{S}}}^{\mathsf{qddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},2},\lambda) + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{hide}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{hide}},\lambda) + \frac{2Q_{\mathrm{S}} + 1}{p} \; .$$

*Proof* (of Lemma 6.9). We consider the following sequence of games:

- Game  $G_{B.5.0}$  (Game  $G_{B.4}$ ): This game is identical to  $G_{B.4}$ .
- Game  $G_{B.5.1}$  (Sample  $u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  instead of  $\mathbb{Z}_p^*$ ): In this game, the signing oracle  $S_1$ , on its j-th query, samples  $u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  instead. Since uniform distributions over  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $\mathbb{Z}_p^*$  have statistical distance of 1/p, over  $Q_S$  queries, we have  $|\Pr[G_{B.5.0}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \Pr[G_{B.5.1}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leq \frac{Q_S}{p}$ .
- Game  $G_{B.5.2}$  (Compute cmt<sub>0</sub> as a commitment of (0,0)): In this game, the key generation generates cmt<sub>0</sub> =  $C_{mac}$ .Commit(mck, (0,0);  $\rho$ ) for  $\rho \leftarrow C_{mac}$ . $\mathcal{R}$  instead.
  - We argue the advantage change via a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{hide}}$  to the hiding property of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . In particular, notice that due to the change in games  $\mathsf{G}_{B.2}$  to  $\mathsf{G}_{B.4}$ , the signing oracles simulate the  $\varSigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  side of the OR-proof, so they do not require ipp to be in the language induced by the linear map  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, x_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Therefore, the reduction can simply simulate the game as in  $\mathsf{G}_{B.5.1}$ . Hence,  $|\mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{G}_{B.5.1}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{G}_{B.5.2}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{hide}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{hide}}, \lambda)$ .
- Game  $G_{B.5.3}$  (Sample  $S_j \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$  when signing info  $\neq$  info\*): In this game, on the j-th query to the signing oracle  $S_1$ , if the common message info does not correspond to the input of the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $H_{pb}$  query (this means that either the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th query has not been made, or the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th query's input is not info), the game samples  $S_j \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$  instead of computing it using msk.

We now show that there exists a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},2}$  such that  $|\mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{B.5.2}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{B.5.3}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen},Q_{\mathsf{S}}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},2},\lambda)$ . The reduction running  $\mathcal{A}$  is defined as follows taking as input the QDDH instance  $(G,A,(B_{j},C_{j})_{j\in[Q_{\mathsf{S}}]})$ : (The [dashed] boxes denote transition from (B.5.2) to (B.5.3), while [highlighted] boxes denote transition from (B.5.3) to (B.5.4).)

Setup pp and vk: The public parameters pp and portions of vk except ipp are computed as in  $G_{B.5.2}$ . We compute ipp by sampling  $[y_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p][x_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p]$ ,  $x_1, y_1, z, \rho_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and setting ipp =  $(C_{\text{mac}}.C(\text{mck}, (0,0); \rho_0), X_1 \leftarrow x_1 F, Y_1 \leftarrow y_1 F, Z = zH)$ 

Signing oracles  $S_1, S_2$ : On the *j*-th  $(j \in [Q_S])$  signing session with tag info, The  $\Sigma_{os}, \Sigma_{mac}, \Sigma_{dleq}$  transcripts are computed as in  $G_{B.5.2}$ , i.e., honestly generated, simulated, and honestly generated, respectively. However, the  $M_{alg}$  tag  $\sigma_{mac,j}$  is computed as follows:

- If info corresponds to the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $\mathsf{H}_{pb}$  query, sample  $u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and set  $U_j \leftarrow u_j G, V_j \leftarrow z U_j,$   $\begin{bmatrix} \bar{S}_j \leftarrow u_j A + u_j x_1 A_{\mathsf{os},j}, T_j \leftarrow u_j y_0 G + u_j y_1 A_{\mathsf{os},j} \end{bmatrix}$   $\begin{bmatrix} \bar{S}_j \leftarrow u_j x_0 G + u_j x_1 A_{\mathsf{os},j}, T_j \leftarrow u_j A + u_j y_1 A_{\mathsf{os},j} \end{bmatrix}.$ 

{40}------------------------------------------------

- Otherwise, recall that  $A_{\text{os},j}$  is computed honestly as  $r_{\text{os},j,0}G + r_{\text{os},j,1}H$  and the reduction knows  $h = \text{dlog}_G H$ , so it knows  $r'_{\text{os},j} = r_{\text{os},j,0} + r_{\text{os},j,1}h$ . It sets  $U_j \leftarrow B_j, V_j \leftarrow zU_j$ ,  $S_j \leftarrow C_j + x_1 r'_{\text{os},j}U_j, T_j \leftarrow y_0U_j + y_1 r'_{\text{os},j}U_j$   $S_j \leftarrow \mathbb{G}, T_j \leftarrow C_j + y_1 r'_{\text{os},j}U_j$ 

Other oracles: They are simulated as in  $G_{\rm B.5.2}$ .

Output bit: Here,  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},2}$  outputs 1 if  $\mathcal{A}$  pass the (efficiently checkable) winning condition in  $\mathbf{G}_{B.5.2}$ . We can easily see that if  $C_j = (\mathsf{dlog}_G A) \cdot B_j$ , the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  within  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},2}$  is identical to its view in  $\mathbf{G}_{B.5.2}$ . Similarly, if  $C_j \leftarrow \mathcal{G}$ ,  $S_j$  is uniformly random for j-th  $S_1$  query with info that is not info\*.

- Game  $G_{B.5.4}$  (Sample  $T_j \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$  when signing info  $\neq$  info\*): In this game, the signing oracle  $S_1$ , on its j-th query, if the common message info does not correspond to the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $H_{pb}$ , the game samples  $T_j \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$  instead of computing it using msk. The advantage change from (B.5.3) to (B.5.4) are justified with the reduction above in [highlighted boxes]. Thus, we have that  $|\Pr[G_{B.5.3}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \Pr[G_{B.5.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leq \operatorname{Adv}_{GGen,Q_S}^{qddh}(\mathcal{B}_{ddh,2},\lambda).$
- Game  $\check{\mathbf{G}}_{\mathrm{B.5.5}}$  (Compute cmt<sub>0</sub> as a commitment of  $(x_0, y_0)$ ): In this game, the key generation generates cmt<sub>0</sub> =  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ .Commit(mck,  $(x_0, y_0)$ ;  $\rho$ ) for  $\rho \leftarrow \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . $\mathcal{R}$  instead. This simply undoes the change made in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.5.2}}$ .

We argue the advantage change via a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{hide}}$  to the hiding property of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . In particular, notice that due to the change in games  $\mathbf{G}_{B.2}$  to  $\mathbf{G}_{B.4}$ , the signing oracles simulate the  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  side of the OR-proof, so they do not require ipp to be in the language induced by the linear map  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, x_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Therefore, the reduction can simply simulate the game as in  $\mathbf{G}_{B.5.4}$ . Hence,  $|\mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{B.5.4}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{B.5.5}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{hide}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{hide}}, \lambda)$ .

- Game  $G_{B.5.6}$  (Sample  $u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*$  instead of  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ ): In this game, the signing oracle  $S_1$ , on its j-th query, samples  $u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*$  instead. Similar to the transition from  $G_{B.5.0}$  to  $G_{B.5.1}$ , we have  $|\Pr[G_{B.5.5}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \Pr[G_{B.5.6}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leq \frac{Q_S}{p}$ .
- Game  $G_{B.5.7}$  (Compute  $U_j \leftarrow u_j F$  instead of  $u_j G$  when signing info  $\neq$  info\*): In this game, on its j-th query the signing oracle  $S_1$  with the input info, if info does not correspond to the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $H_{pb}$  query's input,  $U_j$  and  $V_j$  are now computed as: sample  $u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*$ , set  $U_j \leftarrow u_j F, V_j \leftarrow u_j Z$ . Note that except for when  $F = 0_{\mathbb{G}}$ , the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  is still identical because Z = zF so  $V_j = u_j zF = zU_j$ , so  $|\Pr[G_{B.5.6}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \Pr[G_{B.5.7}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leqslant \frac{1}{p}$ .

Note that  $G_{\rm B.5.7}$  is identical to  $G_{\rm B.5}$ .

Game  $G_{B.6}$  (Compute  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  honestly and simulate  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  for signing on tags info\*): For queries to  $S_1$  and  $S_2$  (with session ID  $j \in [Q_S]$ ) with tag info that corresponds to the  $i_{\mathsf{pb}}^*$ -th  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$  query, this game computes  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  and  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  transcripts as follows:

- $c_{\mathsf{dleq},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p, (A_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, z_{\mathsf{dleq},j}) \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{\mathsf{dleq}}.\mathsf{Sim}(\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{dleq},j}) \text{ where } \mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{dleq},j} = (D_1, D_{2,i_{\mathsf{pb}}^*}, D_{3,i_{\mathsf{pb}}^*}).$
- $(A_{\mathsf{mac},j},\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{mac},j}) \leftarrow \mathcal{E}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathsf{Init}(\mathsf{pp},\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac},j},\mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{mac},j}) \text{ where } \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac},j} = (\mathsf{ipp},A_{\mathsf{os},j},U_j,V_j,S_j,T_j,0_{\mathbb{G}},0_{\mathbb{G}}) \text{ and } \mathbb{w}_{\mathsf{mac},j} = (u_j^{-1},\mathsf{msk}).$
- In S<sub>2</sub>, compute  $c_{\mathsf{mac},j} \leftarrow c_{\mathsf{or},j} c_{\mathsf{dleq}}, z_{\mathsf{mac}} \leftarrow \varSigma_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathsf{Resp}(\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{mac},j}, c_{\mathsf{mac},j}).$

This game simply reverts the changes made in  $G_{B.3}$  and  $G_{B.4}$  but only for signing sessions with tag info\*. Similar to the changes from game  $G_{B.2}$  to  $G_{B.4}$ , we have that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.5}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.6}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

Game  $G_{B.7}$  (Switch  $H_{pb}(info^*)$  to random): In this game, the output of the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th query to  $H_{pb}$  is now switched back to uniformly random, i.e.,  $(D_{2,i_{pb}^*}, D_{3,i_{pb}^*}) \leftarrow \mathbb{G}^2$ . Note that since the  $\Sigma_{dleq}$  transcript for signing on a common message info corresponding to this query is simulated, we do not need the underlying discrete log to compute the transcript. Therefore, one can construct a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{ddh,3}$  from the DDH problem running in time roughly  $T_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$|\mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}^{\mathcal{A}}_{\mathrm{B.6}} \Rightarrow 1] - \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}^{\mathcal{A}}_{\mathrm{B.7}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ddh}}_{\mathsf{GGen}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},3}, \lambda) \; .$$

{41}------------------------------------------------

From this point, we will enforce structure checks on the blinded MAC tags in the forgeries. We will start by introducing inefficient checks that require computing the discrete logarithm of  $\tilde{U}^{(i)}$ . In particular, we want to check that the blinded MAC tags actually satisfy the relation defined by  $\phi_{pp,x_{mac}}^{mac}$  (Equation (2)). Then, later on, relax this check to an efficient check that only uses the MAC secret key msk. This is possible due to the extracted group elements  $(\overline{A}_0^{(i)}, \overline{A}_1^{(i)}, \overline{\Gamma}_{os}^{(i)}, \overline{R}_x^{(i)}, \overline{R}_y^{(i)}, \overline{R}_M^{(i)})$  which embed the blinding factors with the base  $\tilde{U}^{(i)}$ .

Game  $G_{B.8}$  (Enforce (inefficient) check on  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}$  structure): This game introduces a winning condition such that for all forgeries  $i \in [Q_{S,\mathsf{info}}*+1]$ , we require that  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)} = (\widetilde{U}^{(i)} \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}, \widetilde{V}^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_{0}^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_{0}^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_{1}^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_{1}^{(i)})$  satisfy the relation defined by  $\phi^{\mathsf{mac}}$ , i.e., if for  $u^{(i)} = \mathsf{dlog}_{G}\widetilde{U}^{(i)}$ 

$$\widetilde{V}^{(i)} = z\widetilde{U}^{(i)} ,$$

$$(u^{(i)})^{-1}\widetilde{S}_0^{(i)} + \widetilde{S}_1^{(i)} = x_0G + x_1\widetilde{M}^{(i)} ,$$

$$(u^{(i)})^{-1}\widetilde{T}_0^{(i)} + \widetilde{T}_1^{(i)} = y_0G + y_1\widetilde{M}^{(i)} .$$

To bound the advantage change, we will upper bound the probability that  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in game  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.7}}$  but not in this game by invoking soundness of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Hence, we make the following observations.

- With probability 1/p,  $(G, D_1, D_{2,i_{pb}^*}, D_{3,i_{pb}^*})$  will be a DLEQ tuple, otherwise, it is not a valid statement for  $\Sigma_{\text{dleq}}$ . Then, if it is not a valid statement, by special-soundness of  $\Sigma_{\text{dleq}}$ , there is only one  $\widetilde{c}_{\text{dleq}}$  that allows  $\mathcal{A}$  to produce a valid response.
- Moreover, if  $F \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}$  (except with probability 1/p) and due to perfectly strong binding of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ , ipp and  $\widetilde{U}^{(i)}$  statistically fixes the underlying witness  $((u^{(i)})^{-1}, x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z, \rho_0)$  of the statement  $\mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)} = (\mathsf{ipp}, \widetilde{U}^{(i)} \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}, \widetilde{V}^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_0^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_0^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}_1^{(i)}, \widetilde{T}_1^{(i)})$ . Note that if  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)}$  is not in the language, no such witness would exist. Therefore, if  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)}$  does not satisfy the introduced checks,  $\mathsf{x}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)}$  is not in the language induced by the map  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp},\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)}}^{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Again, via 2-special-soundness of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$ , there is only one  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  that allows  $\mathcal{A}$  to produce a valid response.

Therefore, except for the bad cases, there is at most 1/p probability of a bad challenge  $\tilde{c}_{or}$  being sampled per each RO query; hence, via the union bound over the bad cases  $(F = 0_{\mathbb{G}}, (G, D_1, D_{2,i_{pb}^*}, D_{3,i_{pb}^*})$  is a DLEQ tuple, and bad challenge), we have

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.7}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.8}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] + \frac{Q_{\mathsf{H}} + 2}{p}$$
.

Game  $G_{B.9}$  (Enforce (inefficient) check on  $cmt_{rnd}$  structure): This game introduces a winning condition such that for all forgeries  $i \in [Q_{S,info}*+1]$ , the committed values of  $cmt_{rnd}^{(i)}$  satisfies certain relations. In particular, for each i, we let

$$(\pmb{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} = (\alpha_0^{(i)}, \alpha_1^{(i)}), \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i)}, r_x^{(i)}, r_y^{(i)}, r_M^{(i)}) \leftarrow \mathsf{dlog}_{\widetilde{U}^{(i)}}(\overline{A}_0^{(i)}, \overline{A}_1^{(i)}, \overline{T}_{\text{os}}^{(i)}, \overline{R}_x^{(i)}, \overline{R}_M^{(i)}) \,,$$

and check the following equations

$$\begin{split} \overline{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} &= \widetilde{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} - \phi_{\text{pp},W}^{\text{os}}(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) + \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \cdot W \;, \\ \widetilde{M}^{(i)} &= \overline{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} + r_M^{(i)} F \;, \\ \widetilde{S}_1^{(i)} &= r_x^{(i)} G + r_M^{(i)} X_1 \;, \quad \widetilde{T}_1^{(i)} = r_y^{(i)} G + r_M^{(i)} Y_1 \;. \end{split}$$

We now argue the change in advantage from the previous game. We note that due to extractability of of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ , if  $\mathsf{cmt}^{(i)}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  does not satisfy the above check, then  $\mathsf{x}^{(i)}_{\mathsf{rnd}} = (W, X_1, Y_1, \widetilde{A}^{(i)}_{\mathsf{os}}, \mathsf{cmt}^{(i)}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{M}^{(i)}, \widetilde{U}^{(i)}, \widetilde{S}^{(i)}_1, \widetilde{T}^{(i)}_1)$  is

{42}------------------------------------------------

not a valid statement for  $\Sigma_{rnd}$ . Therefore, via special-soundness, there is only one bad challenge  $\tilde{c}_{rnd}$  possible per each H query; then, with the union bound over all queries, we have that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.8}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.9}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] + \frac{Q_{\mathsf{H}}}{p}$$
.

Game  $G_{B.10}$  (Relax the checks from  $G_{B.8}, G_{B.9}$  to be efficient): For each  $i \in [Q_{S,info}* + 1]$ , the game computes

<span id="page-42-2"></span>
$$C_M^{(i)} \leftarrow (\widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{os},0}^{(i)} + \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{os},1}^{(i)} \cdot h - \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)} \cdot w') \widetilde{U}^{(i)} - \overline{A}_0^{(i)} - h \cdot \overline{A}_1^{(i)} + w' \overline{\Gamma}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i)} . \tag{9}$$

and checks

<span id="page-42-1"></span><span id="page-42-0"></span>
$$\widetilde{V}^{(i)} = z\widetilde{U}^{(i)} , \qquad (10)$$

$$\widetilde{S}_0 + \overline{R}_x^{(i)} = x_0 \widetilde{U}^{(i)} + x_1 C_M^{(i)} ,$$
(11)

$$\widetilde{T}_0 + \overline{R}_y^{(i)} = y_0 \widetilde{U}^{(i)} + y_1 C_M^{(i)}$$
 (12)

It also stops making the inefficient checks introduced in  $G_{B.8}$  and  $G_{B.9}$ . Intuitively, we make these changes to allow the game hops (via DDH) to still efficiently check specific structure of the blinded MAC tags in the signatures while not having to compute the discrete log of  $\tilde{U}^{(i)}$ . This particular step is also why we need to commit to group elements in cmt<sub>rnd</sub> with base generator  $\tilde{U}$  in our scheme instead of G.

Due to the constraints from games  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.8}}$  and  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.9}}$ , this is only relaxing the winning condition, i.e., if the prior checks on  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}^{(i)}$  and  $\mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}^{(i)}$  pass, the check in this game also passes. More formally, from the checks in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.8}}$ , (10) follows trivially, and we can see that

$$\begin{split} C_M^{(i)} &= (\widetilde{z}_{\text{os},0}^{(i)} + \widetilde{z}_{\text{os},1}^{(i)} \cdot h - \widetilde{c}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \cdot w') \widetilde{U}^{(i)} - \overline{A}_0^{(i)} - h \cdot \overline{A}_1^{(i)} + w' \overline{\Gamma}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \;, \\ &= \mathsf{dlog}_G(\widetilde{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) \widetilde{U}^{(i)} - \mathsf{dlog}_G(\phi_{\mathsf{pp},W}^{\mathsf{os}}(\alpha_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) + \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \cdot W) \widetilde{U}^{(i)} \\ &= u^{(i)} (\widetilde{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} + \phi_{\mathsf{pp},W}^{\mathsf{os}}(\alpha_{\text{os}}^{(i)}) + \gamma_{\text{os}}^{(i)} \cdot W) = u^{(i)} \overline{A}_{\text{os}}^{(i)} = u^{(i)} \widetilde{M}^{(i)} - u^{(i)} r_M^{(i)} F \;. \end{split}$$

The second equation follows from validity of  $\Sigma_{os}$  transcript in  $\sigma^{(i)}$ , and the checks in  $\mathbf{G}_{B.8}$ . The third follows from  $u^{(i)}G = \widetilde{U}^{(i)}$ , and the last follows from the check on  $\widetilde{M}^{(i)}$  in  $\mathbf{G}_{B.8}$ . Thus,

$$(u^{(i)})^{-1}\widetilde{S}_{0}^{(i)} + \widetilde{S}_{1}^{(i)} = x_{0}G + x_{1}\widetilde{M}^{(i)}$$

$$\widetilde{S}_{0}^{(i)} + u^{(i)}\widetilde{S}_{1}^{(i)} = x_{0}\widetilde{U}^{(i)} + x_{1}u^{(i)}\widetilde{M}^{(i)}$$

$$\widetilde{S}_{0}^{(i)} + u^{(i)}(r_{x}^{(i)}G + r_{M}^{(i)}X_{1}) = x_{0}\widetilde{U}^{(i)} + x_{1}u^{(i)}\widetilde{M}^{(i)}$$

$$\widetilde{S}_{0}^{(i)} + \overline{R}_{x}^{(i)} + x_{1}r_{M}^{(i)}u^{(i)}F = x_{0}\widetilde{U}^{(i)} + x_{1}C_{M}^{(i)} + x_{1}r_{M}^{(i)}u^{(i)}F$$

$$\widetilde{S}_{0}^{(i)} + \overline{R}_{x}^{(i)} = x_{0}\widetilde{U}^{(i)} + x_{1}C_{M}^{(i)}.$$

The third line follows from the checks introduced in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B},9}$ , the fourth follows from the above equation on  $C_M^{(i)}$ , and the fifth follows from cancelling the terms from both sides. Similar equalities apply to  $\widetilde{T}_0^{(i)}$  and  $\widetilde{T}_1^{(i)}$ . Hence, we obtain

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{B,9}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{B,10}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$$
.

Game  $G_{B.11}$  (Switch  $H(info^*)$  to be DLEQ instance): In this game, the output of the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th query to  $H_{pb}$  is now switched to sampling  $a_{i_{pb}^*} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and set  $(D_{2,i_{pb}^*}, D_{3,i_{pb}^*}) \leftarrow (a_{i_{pb}^*}G, a_{i_{pb}^*}D_1)$ . Note that since the  $\Sigma_{dleq}$  transcript for signing on a tag info\* is now simulated, we do not need the underlying discrete log to compute the transcript. Also, the winning condition is efficiently checkable using msk. Therefore, one can construct a straightforward reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{ddh,4}$  from the DDH problem running in time roughly  $t_{\mathcal{A}}$  such that

$$|\text{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}.10}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \text{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}.11}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{GGen}}^{\mathsf{ddh}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{ddh},4}, \lambda) \;.$$

{43}------------------------------------------------

Game  $G_{B.12}$  (Compute  $\Sigma_{dleq}$  honestly and simulate  $\Sigma_{mac}$  for signing on all tags): In this game, we revert the changes made in  $G_{B.6}$ , such that all signing oracle queries now generate the  $\Sigma_{dleq}$  and  $\Sigma_{mac}$  transcripts by honestly computing using the corresponding  $a_i$  witness of  $H_{pb}(info_i)$  and simulating, respectively. With similar arguments from  $G_{B.5}$  to  $G_{B.6}$ , we have that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{B,11}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{B,12}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

Game  $G_{B.13}$  (Change how  $A_{os}$  are sampled when signing info\*): For signing session  $j \in [Q_S]$  where info is the  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $H_{pb}$  query, we sample  $r'_{os,j}, r_{os,j,1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and set  $A_{os,j} \leftarrow r'_{os,j}G$ , while we set  $r_{os,j,0} \leftarrow r'_{os,j} - r_{os,j,1}h$  and  $\rho_{os,j}^* \leftarrow (r_{os,j,0}, r_{os,j,1})$ . Note that the view of the adversary remains the same (since we only change the sampling order which is initially sampling  $r_{os,j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  and setting  $r'_{os,j} = r_{os,j,0} + hr_{os,j,1}$ ). Thus, we have

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{R12}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{R13}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

Game  $G_{B.14}$  (Sample all  $A_{os}$  in advance): This game samples randomness that will be used in the simulation in advance. In particular, it prepares two sets of randomness to be used in computing the MAC tag  $\sigma_{mac}$  and the  $\Sigma_{os}$  nonce  $A_{os}$  in signing sessions corresponding and not corresponding to  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $H_{pb}$  query, respectively:

$$(\rho_{S,j}^* = (u_j^* \in \mathbb{Z}_p^*, r'_{\mathsf{os},j} \in \mathbb{Z}_p, r_{\mathsf{os},j,1} \in \mathbb{Z}_p))_{j \in [Q_S]},$$
  
$$(\rho_{S,j} = (u_j \in \mathbb{Z}_p, S_j \in \mathbb{G}, T_j \in \mathbb{G}, \rho_{\mathsf{os},j}))_{j \in [Q_S]}.$$

The game also keeps track of counters J and  $J^*$  (initially 0) which will be incremented when  $S_1$  queries with info  $\neq$  info<sup>\*</sup> and info<sup>\*</sup>, respectively, are made. In particular, each case the game does the following to compute  $\sigma_{\text{mac}}$  and  $A_{\text{os}}$  on the query info to  $S_1$ :

- info does not correspond to  $i_{pb}^*$ -th  $H_{pb}$  query: Increment J. Set  $\sigma_{mac} = (U \leftarrow u_J F, V \leftarrow u_J Z, S_J, T_J)$  and  $A_{os} \leftarrow \Sigma_{os}.Init(W, \boldsymbol{w}; \rho_{os,J})$ .
- info corresponds to  $i_{\text{pb}}$ -th  $\mathsf{H}_{\text{pb}}$  query: Increment  $J^*$ . Set  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}} = (U \leftarrow u_J^*G, V \leftarrow zU, S \leftarrow u_J^*(x_0 + x_1r'_{\mathsf{os},J^*})G, T \leftarrow u_J^*(y_0 + y_1r'_{\mathsf{os},J^*})G)$  and  $A_{\mathsf{os}} \leftarrow \varSigma_{\mathsf{os}}.\mathsf{Init}(W, \boldsymbol{w}; \rho_{\mathsf{os},J^*}^*)$  where  $\rho_{\mathsf{os},J}^* = (r'_{\mathsf{os},J^*} r_{\mathsf{os},J^*,1}h, r_{\mathsf{os},J,1})$ .

Then,  $\rho_{S,J}$  and  $\rho_{S,J*}^*$  will be used to compute  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  and  $A_{\mathsf{os}}$  according to the cases. Finally, this game introduces an abort at the end of the game if  $\overline{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i^*)} \in \{r'_{\mathsf{os},j}G\}_{j \in [Q_S]}$ .

The purpose generating the nonces and tags beforehand is to prepare for the rewinding reduction. In particular, we note the first run of  $\mathcal{A}$  will (statistically) fix a MAC forgery for a fresh nonce  $\overline{\mathcal{A}}_{os}^{(i^*)}$ . Then, consider the situation when the reduction makes extra MAC tag queries in the second run of  $\mathcal{A}$ , it is possible that a tag was given for this nonce; and thus, invalidating the freshness of the MAC forgery. The abort is introduced to avoid a situation where  $\mathcal{A}$  does not make all of its  $Q_S$  signing queries on info\*. Indeed, the prepared nonces and tags will not be given to  $\mathcal{A}$ , but we still want to ensure that we can find a fresh MAC tag and nonce from  $\mathcal{A}$ 's forgeries—which should not correspond to any of the prepared but unused tags and nonces.

Despite the change, the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  remains the same, because we only move the sampling of the values to the start. The only change in advantage is due to the introduced abort. Since by definition of  $i^*$ ,  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i^*)} \neq r'_{os,j}G$  for  $1 \leq j < \ell$ , we only have to consider when  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i^*)} = r'_{os,j}G$  for  $\ell + 1 \leq j \leq Q_S$ . However,  $r'_{os,j}$  for  $\ell \leq j \leq Q_S$  are uniformly random and hidden from the adversary, since these are prepared random values that were not given to  $\mathcal{A}$  as it only makes  $\ell - 1$  queries on info\*. Therefore, the probability of such abort occurring is at most  $Q_S/p$  via the union bound over  $\ell \leq j \leq Q_S$ . Therefore,

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.13}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.14}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] + \frac{Q_{\mathrm{S}}}{p}$$
.

<span id="page-43-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>7</sup> Recall that the index  $i^* \in [\ell]$  corresponds to a forgery where the extracted  $\overline{A}_{os}^{(i^*)}$  is one of the nonces not used in the signing sessions on info\*. This exists due to the extracted nonces being distinct and the pigeonhole principle.

{44}------------------------------------------------

Fig. 15. Wrapper algorithm  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$  for the proof of Lemma 6.3. The oracles simulation are given in Figure 16. We denote internal states of  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$  info $[\cdot]$ , str $[\cdot]$  for mappings from indices  $i \in [Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]$  and  $i \in [Q_{\mathsf{H}}]$  to the i-th query to  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$  and  $\mathsf{H}$ , respectively; additionally,  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}[\cdot]$ ,  $\mathsf{H}[\cdot]$  are mappings from query to output of the corresponding RO. We assume that the tuple  $(\mathbb{G}, p, G)$  is implicit in  $\mathsf{pp}$ .

To bound the advantage of  $\mathcal{A}$  in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.14}}$ , we will rewind the adversary to extract (via special-soundness of  $\Sigma_{\mathrm{rnd}}$ ) the underlying randomization on  $\widetilde{M}^{(i^*)}$  and  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathrm{mac}}^{(i^*)}$  and then construct a reduction to UF-RMA of  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ . We establish this in the following lemma.

<span id="page-44-0"></span>Lemma 6.10 (Forking for NonceDist). There exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  in game UF-RMA running in time  $T_{alg} \approx 2T_{\mathcal{A}}$  making  $Q_{S}$  queries to the Tag such that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.14}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{H}} \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}}^{\mathsf{ufrma}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathrm{alg}}, \lambda)} + \frac{Q_{\mathrm{H}}}{p} \; .$$

Proof (of Lemma 6.10). The proof follows the following steps: (1) Define a wrapper algorithm  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$ , (2) Construct a reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  against UF-RMA game of  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  that rewinds  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$ , (3) Analyze  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  via the forking lemma.

WRAPPER  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$ . The wrapper  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$  (defined in Figures 15 and 16) simulates the game  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{B.14}}$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ . In particular, it takes as input the public parameters  $\mathsf{pp}$  as generated in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{A.14}}$ ,  $\mathsf{ipp}$  generated via  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{KeyGen}$  (but without access to  $\mathsf{msk}$ ), extraction trapdoor  $\mathsf{td}$ , witness  $\boldsymbol{w} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  for  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{os}}$ , discrete logarithm  $h \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , and prepared randomness  $((\rho_{\mathsf{S},j}^*, \rho_{\mathsf{S},j}, \rho_{\mathsf{S},j}, \rho_{\mathsf{S},j})_{j \in [Q_{\mathsf{S}}]}, (a_i)_{i \in [Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]}, (\tilde{c}_i)_{i \in [Q_{\mathsf{H}}]}, i_{\mathsf{pb}}^*)$  to be used for oracle simulation along with challenges  $\boldsymbol{h} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{Q_{\mathsf{H}}}$ . It then runs  $\mathcal{A}$  and simulates the game as follows:

Input to A: The wrapper forwards pp and  $vk = (ipp, W = w_0G + w_1H)$  to A.

Random oracles  $H, H_{pb}$ :  $(\tilde{c}_i \in \mathbb{Z}_p^2)_{i \in [Q_H]}$  and h are used to simulate H where the i-th query is replied with  $(\tilde{c}_i, h_i) \in \mathbb{Z}_p^3$ , while  $a_i$  is used to simulate  $H_{pb}$  where the i-th query is replied with  $a_i(G, D_1)$ .

15: return (\overline{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac},\mathsf{cnt}_{\mathrm{S}}}, A_{\mathsf{os},\mathsf{cnt}_{\mathrm{S}}}, A_{\mathsf{mac},\mathsf{cnt}_{\mathrm{S}}}, A_{\mathsf{dleq},\mathsf{cnt}_{\mathrm{S}}})
```

Fig. 16. Oracle simulation by  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$  extended from Figure 15. We simplify the description of  $S_2$  be removing the sid tracking and assume that the second time an sid is queried to  $S_2$ ,  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{pr-cr}}$  simply return  $\bot$ .

Signing oracles  $S_1, S_2$ : Throughout the simulation,  $i_{pb}^*$  corresponds to the guessed index of info\*. Counters  $J, J^*$  are incremented as in  $G_{A.14}$ .

- $\rho_{S,j}^* = (\sigma_{\mathsf{mac},j}, r'_{\mathsf{os},j}, r_{\mathsf{os},j,0})$  is used to compute  $A_{\mathsf{os}}$  in j-th signing session where  $\mathsf{info}^*$  is queried. However, we note that  $\rho_{S,j}^*$  already contains precomputed  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  tag  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac},j}$ , which will come from the Tag oracle in our reduction.
- $\rho_{S,j} = (u_j, S_j, T_j, \rho_{os,j})$  is used to compute the tag  $(u_J F, u_J Z, S_J, T_J)$  and  $A_{os}$  for the j-th signing session where info  $\neq$  info\* as in  $\mathbf{G}_{B.14}$ .
- $\rho_{\Sigma,j}$  will be used in the j-th signing session (including both signing info\* and info  $\neq$  info\*) to compute  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  and  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  transcripts.

Output of  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$ : The wrapper checks that the event NonceDist actually occurs and that there is an index  $i^*$  where  $\overline{A}_{\mathsf{os}}^{(i^*)}$  does not correspond to the prepared values  $r'_{\mathsf{os},j}G$  as checked in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{B}.14}$ . Then, it outputs the corresponding index  $I \in [Q_{\mathsf{H}}]$  to the H query in the verification of the  $i^*$ -th forgery along with  $\sigma^{(i^*)}$  If NonceDist does not occur, it returns  $\bot$ .

We note that the wrapper does not check the additional winning condition introduced in  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.10}}$ . This is due to the reduction not having access to the MAC secret key msk. However, if  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in game  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.14}}$ , then the output  $(I, \sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho_{\mathcal{A}})$  also satisfy the checks in Equations (10) to (12). In particular, if we let

$$\begin{split} & \sigma = (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{T}_1), \mathrm{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}}) \;, \\ & (\overline{A}_0, \overline{A}_1, \overline{\varGamma}_{\mathsf{os}}, \overline{R}_x, \overline{R}_y, \overline{R}_M, \overline{A}_{\mathsf{os}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}.\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{td}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}) \;, \end{split}$$

we have that

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B.14}}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \leqslant \Pr_{\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}, \rho_{\mathcal{A}}} \begin{bmatrix} I \neq \bot & \tilde{V} = z\widetilde{U} & \wedge \\ \widetilde{S}_{0} + \overline{R}_{x} = x_{0}\widetilde{U} + x_{1}C_{M} & \wedge \\ \widetilde{T}_{0} + \overline{R}_{y} = y_{0}\widetilde{U} + y_{1}C_{M} \end{bmatrix} (I, \sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho_{\mathcal{A}}) \end{bmatrix}$$

where

<span id="page-45-1"></span>
$$C_M \leftarrow (\widetilde{z}_{os,0} + \widetilde{z}_{os,1} \cdot h - \widetilde{c}_{os} \cdot w')\widetilde{U} - \overline{A}_0 - h \cdot \overline{A}_1 + w'\overline{\Gamma}_{os}, \qquad (13)$$

as in Equation (9). Due to perfect strong binding of  $C_{mac}$ , the underlying secret keys  $x_0, y_0, x_1, y_1, z$  are fixed in the ipp. Denote such event on the output  $\sigma$  as Good. For our reduction's analysis, we define an additional

{46}------------------------------------------------

```
Alg. \mathcal{B}_{\mathrm{alg}}^{\mathrm{Tag}}(\mathsf{mpp},\mathsf{ipp}):
  1: h \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p ; H \leftarrow hG ; (bck, td) \leftarrow \mathbb{C}_{rnd}.ExtSetup(\mathbb{G}, p, G) ; w \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2
   2: pp \leftarrow (H, mpp = (F, mck), bck)
   3: for j \in [Q_S]:
   4: (r'_{os,j}, \sigma_{mac,j}) \leftarrow \text{Tag}() // Set up MAC tags
                    u_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_n^* ; S_i, T_i \leftarrow \mathbb{G}
   5:
   6: r_{os,j,1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p ; \rho_{os,j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2
  7: \rho_{\mathsf{mac},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{6} \times \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathcal{R} ; \rho_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{mac},j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}
  8: \rho_{S,j}^* \leftarrow (\sigma_{\mathsf{mac},j}, r'_{\mathsf{os},j}, r_{\mathsf{os},j,1}) ; \rho_{S,j} \leftarrow (u_j, S_j, T_j, \rho_{\mathsf{os},j})
   9: \rho_{\Sigma,j} \leftarrow (\rho_{\mathsf{mac},j}, \rho_{\mathsf{dleq},j}, c_{\mathsf{mac},j})
10: \quad a_1, \dots, a_{Q_{\mathsf{pb}}} \leftarrow \$ \, \mathbb{Z}_p \, ; \widetilde{c}_1, \dots, \widetilde{c}_{Q_{\mathsf{H}}} \leftarrow \$ \, \mathbb{Z}_p^2 \, ; i_{\mathsf{pb}}^{ \bigstar} \leftarrow \$ \, [Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]
11: \quad \mathsf{inp} \leftarrow (\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{ipp}, \mathsf{td}, \boldsymbol{w}, h, (\rho_{\mathrm{S}, j}^{\bigstar}, \rho_{\mathrm{S}, j}, \rho_{\Sigma, j})_{j \in [Q_{\mathrm{S}}]}, (a_i)_{i \in [Q_{\mathrm{pb}}]}, (\tilde{c}_i)_{i \in [Q_{\mathrm{H}}]}, i_{\mathrm{pb}}^{\bigstar})
12: (b, \sigma, \sigma') \leftarrow \$ \operatorname{Fork}^{A_{\operatorname{NonceDist}}}(\operatorname{inp})
13: if b = 0 then return \bot
14: parse \sigma = (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\})
15: parse \sigma' = (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}'_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}})
16: parse \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)
17: \mathbb{X}_{\mathsf{rnd}} = (W = w_0 G + w_1 H, X_1, Y_1, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{M}, \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_1)
18: (\alpha_0, \alpha_1, \gamma_{os}, r_x, r_y, r_M, \rho_{rnd}) \leftarrow \Sigma_{rnd}.\mathsf{Ext}(\mathbb{X}_{rnd}, \widetilde{A}_{rnd}, \widetilde{c}_{rnd}, \widetilde{c}_{rnd}, \widetilde{c}_{rnd}', \widetilde{c}_{rnd}', \widetilde{c}_{rnd}')
19: \quad w' \leftarrow w_0 + w_1 h
20: m^* \leftarrow \widetilde{z}_{os,0} + \widetilde{z}_{os,1}h - \widetilde{c}_{os}w' - \alpha_0 - \alpha_1h + \gamma_{os}w'
21: \sigma_{\text{alg}}^* \leftarrow (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0 + r_x \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{T}_0 + r_y \widetilde{U})
22: return (m^*, \sigma_{\text{alg}}^*)
```

**Fig. 17.** Reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$ . We assume that the tuple  $(\mathbb{G}, p, G)$  is implicit in mpp.

inefficient wrapper  $\mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$  which runs  $\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}$  but also checks for Good on the output, and return  $\bot$  if it does not occur; hence,

```
\begin{split} & \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}, \rho_{\mathcal{A}}} \big[ \bot \neq (I, \sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho_{\mathcal{A}}) \big] \\ & := \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}, \rho_{\mathcal{A}}} \big[ \bot \neq (I, \sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho_{\mathcal{A}}) \ \land \ \mathsf{Good} \big] \geqslant \mathsf{Pr} \big[ \mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{B}.14}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \big] \ . \end{split}
```

REDUCTION  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$ . Our reduction  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  (given in Figure 17) takes as input mpp and ipp from the UF-RMA game and runs  $\mathcal{A}_{NonceDist}$  twice (via the forking algorithm Fork  $\mathcal{A}_{NonceDist}$ ), preparing its input inp as follows:

- Sample  $H \in \mathbb{G}$  while knowing  $\mathsf{dlog}_G H$ , bck along with an extraction trapdoor td from  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . ExtSetup, the Okamoto-Schnorr witness  $\boldsymbol{w} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}[Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]$  and setup  $W \leftarrow w_0 G + w_1 H$ , and  $i_{\mathsf{pb}}^* \leftarrow \mathbb{F}[Q_{\mathsf{pb}}]$ .
- Randomness for signing info\*: Call the Tag oracle to setup the  $Q_S$  randomness  $r'_{os,j}$  and the corresponding  $M_{alg}$  tag  $\sigma_{mac,j}$ . Also, sample  $r_{os,j,1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ .
- Randomness for signing info  $\neq$  info\*: Sample  $u_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^*, S_j, T_j \leftarrow \mathbb{G}$  and  $\rho_{os,j} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2$ .
- Randomness for  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$ ,  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$ : Sample  $c_{\mathsf{mac},j}$ ,  $\rho_{\mathsf{mac},j}$  and  $\rho_{\mathsf{dleq},j}$  to be used for computing the  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$ ,  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  transcripts in signing.
- RO outputs: Sample  $a_1, \ldots, a_{Q_{\mathsf{pb}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p, \widetilde{c}_1, \ldots, \widetilde{c}_{Q_{\mathsf{H}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  and  $\boldsymbol{h} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{Q_{\mathsf{H}}}$ .

It runs  $Fork^{A_{NonceDist}}(inp)$ , where inp is sampled as above, and aborts if the forking algorithm is unsuccessful. Otherwise, it parses the outputs of Fork as

$$\begin{split} \sigma &= (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}}) \;, \\ \sigma' &= (\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, (\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{xxx}}, \widetilde{z}'_{\mathsf{xxx}})_{\mathsf{xxx} \in \{\mathsf{os}, \mathsf{mac}, \mathsf{dleq}, \mathsf{rnd}\}}) \;, \\ \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}} &= (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{S}_1, \widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{T}_1) \end{split}$$

{47}------------------------------------------------

Note that  $\widetilde{M}$ ,  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ ,  $\mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ ,  $\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{xxx}}$  are shared since they are contained in the same query to H within the two runs due to the success condition of Fork. Also, with  $h_I \neq h_I'$ ,  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}} \neq \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ . Then, it uses the extractor of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  to extract the underlying witness denoted  $(\alpha_0, \alpha_1, \gamma_{\mathsf{os}}, r_x, r_y, r_M)$  from the two valid transcripts  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}})$  and  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}'_{\mathsf{rnd}})$ . Finally, the reduction returns the following values as  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  forgery:

$$m^* = \widetilde{z}_{os,0} + \widetilde{z}_{os,1}h - \widetilde{c}_{os}w' - \alpha_0 - \alpha_1h + \gamma_{os}w',$$
  
$$\sigma_{alg}^* = (\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{V}, \widetilde{S}_0 + r_x\widetilde{U}, \widetilde{T}_0 + r_y\widetilde{U}).$$

Analysis of  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$ . First, recall that by the definition of  $\mathcal{A}_{NonceDist}$ , the underlying  $\overline{A}_{os}$  extracted from cmt<sub>rnd</sub> does not correspond to any  $\{r'_{os,j}G\}_{j\in[Q_S]}$ . Hence, by definition of the mapping  $\phi_{pp,x_{rnd}}^{rnd}$  and the extracted witnesses, we have

$$\begin{split} \overline{A}_{\text{os}} &= \widetilde{A}_{\text{os}} - \alpha_0 G - \alpha_1 H + \gamma_{\text{os}} W \\ &= \phi_{\text{pp}, x_{\text{os}}}^{\text{os}} (\widetilde{z}_{\text{os}}) - \widetilde{c}_{\text{os}} W - \alpha_0 G - \alpha_1 H + \gamma_{\text{os}} W \\ &= \widetilde{z}_{\text{os}, 0} G + \widetilde{z}_{\text{os}, 1} H - \widetilde{c}_{\text{os}} W - \alpha_0 G - \alpha_1 H + \gamma_{\text{os}} W \\ &= (\widetilde{z}_{\text{os}, 0} + \widetilde{z}_{\text{os}, 1} h - \widetilde{c}_{\text{os}} w' - \alpha_0 - \alpha_1 h + \gamma_{\text{os}} w') G = m^* G \;. \end{split}$$

The second equality follows from the verification equation of  $\Sigma_{os}$ . Thus,  $m^*$  is a fresh message not output from Tag before.

Therefore, we only need to identify an event where  $\mathcal{B}_{alg}$  outputs a valid  $\sigma_{alg}^*$  for  $m^*$ . Recall the checks in the event Good, i.e., we have

$$\widetilde{V} = z\widetilde{U}$$
,  $\widetilde{S}_0 + \overline{R}_x = x_0\widetilde{U} + x_1C_M$ ,  $\widetilde{T}_0 + \overline{R}_y = y_0\widetilde{U} + y_1C_M$ .

Here, by special soundness of  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ , the extracted witness satisfies  $(\alpha_0, \alpha_1, \gamma_{\mathsf{os}}, r_x, r_y, r_M)\widetilde{U} = (\overline{A}_0, \overline{A}_1, \overline{\Gamma}_{\mathsf{os}}, \overline{R}_x, \overline{R}_y, \overline{R}_M)$ . Thus, via Equation (13), we have that

$$C_{M} = (\widetilde{z}_{os,0} + \widetilde{z}_{os,1} \cdot h - \widetilde{c}_{os} \cdot w')\widetilde{U} - \overline{A}_{0} - h \cdot \overline{A}_{1} + w'\overline{\Gamma}_{os}$$

$$= (\widetilde{z}_{os,0} + \widetilde{z}_{os,1} \cdot h - \widetilde{c}_{os} \cdot w' - \alpha_{0} - \alpha_{1}h + \gamma_{os}w')\widetilde{U} = m^{*}\widetilde{U}.$$

Therefore, the reduction's output satisfies

$$\widetilde{S}_0 + \overline{R}_x = x_0 \widetilde{U} + x_1 C_M$$

$$\widetilde{S}_0 + r_x \widetilde{U} = (x_0 + x_1 m^*) \widetilde{U}.$$

Similarly,  $\widetilde{T}_0 + r_y \widetilde{U} = (y_0 + y_1 m^*) \widetilde{U}$ , meaning that  $\sigma_{\text{alg}}^*$  is valid for  $m^*$  with respect to the underlying msk. Thus, if in both runs of  $\mathcal{A}_{\text{NonceDist}}$  within Fork, the output indices I = I' and the event Good occurs (i.e., the additional wrapper  $\mathcal{A}'_{\text{NonceDist}}$  outputs  $I = I' \neq \bot$ ),  $\mathcal{B}_{\text{alg}}$  wins in the UF-RMA game. Therefore,

$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}}^{\mathsf{ufrma}}(\mathcal{B}_{\mathrm{alg}},\lambda) \geqslant \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp}} \big[ \mathsf{Fork}^{\mathcal{A}_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}'}(\mathsf{inp}) \neq \bot \big] \geqslant \mathsf{Pr} \big[ \mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}.14}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \big] \left( \frac{\mathsf{Pr} \big[ \mathbf{G}_{\mathrm{B}.14}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1 \big]}{Q_{\mathsf{H}}} - \frac{1}{p} \right) \; ,$$

where the last inequality follows from Lemma 2.19 and that  $\mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp},\boldsymbol{h},\rho_{\mathcal{A}}}[\bot \neq (I,\sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}'_{\mathsf{NonceDist}}(\mathsf{inp},\boldsymbol{h};\rho_{\mathcal{A}})] \geqslant \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}^{\mathcal{A}}_{\mathsf{B},14} \Rightarrow 1]$ . Note that  $\mathcal{B}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  runs in time roughly  $2T_{\mathcal{A}}$ , concluding the proof.

# <span id="page-47-0"></span>7 Blindness Proof of BS<sub>alg</sub>

In this section, we show Theorem 3.6. Recall that  $Q_{\mathsf{H}}$  (resp.  $Q_{\mathsf{pb}}$ ) denotes the number of hash queries to  $\mathsf{H}$  (resp.  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$ ), including the queries induced by the blindness game. Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be an adversary against the blindness game of  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ , running in time  $t_{\mathcal{A}}$ . Let us consider the following sequence of games, where we denote

{48}------------------------------------------------

 $\Pr[\mathbf{G}^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]$  (omitting the parameter  $\lambda$ ) as the probability of the game  $\mathbf{G}$  outputting 1 after interacting with adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ .

Game  $G_0$  (Original blindness game): This game is the original blindness game, i.e., the game runs  $pp \leftarrow S_{alg}.Setup(1^{\lambda})$ , samples  $b \leftarrow S(0,1)$  and interacts with A on input pp simulating the oracles Init,  $U_1$  and  $U_2$  honestly. When A outputs b', the game outputs 1 iff b' = b. By definition, we have

$$\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{blind}}_{\mathsf{BS}_{\mathrm{alg}}}(\mathcal{A},\lambda) = \left|\mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_0^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \frac{1}{2}\right|.$$

In the following, we assume that  $U \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}$  and that the  $\Sigma$ -protocol transcripts issued by the adversary verify. This is without loss of generality, as these checks are performed by  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{U}_2$ ; if a check fails, then the game outputs  $(\bot, \bot)$  for both signing sessions.

Game G<sub>1</sub> (Abort if H was queried before  $\mathcal{A}$  recevied  $(\sigma_0, \sigma_1)$ ): When the game queries in<sub>H</sub> :=  $(\widetilde{M}, \widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \mathrm{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{os}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \mu, \mathsf{info})$  to H in oracle U<sub>1</sub>, the game aborts if in<sub>H</sub> was already queried to H by  $\mathcal{A}$ . Further, the game also aborts in oracle H if in<sub>H</sub> is later queried by  $\mathcal{A}$  before it obtains  $(\sigma_0, \sigma_1)$ .

Observe that  $\widetilde{U} = \beta U \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}}$  and that the values  $r_M, r_x, r_y \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  are information-theoretically hidden from  $\mathcal{A}$  before obtaining  $(\sigma_0, \sigma_1)$ . As the values  $\widetilde{M} = A_{os} + r_M F, \widetilde{S}_0 = \beta S - r_x \widetilde{U}, \widetilde{T}_0 = \beta T - r_y \widetilde{U}$  are uniform over  $\mathbb{G}$ , the probability that the game aborts is at most  $Q_H/p^3$ . As there are at most two non-aborting calls to  $U_1$ , we have

$$\left| \Pr[\mathbf{G}_0^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \Pr[\mathbf{G}_1^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \right| \leqslant \frac{2Q_{\mathsf{H}}}{p^3}.$$

Game  $G_2$  (Simulate  $(\widetilde{A}_{rnd}, \widetilde{c}_{rnd}, \widetilde{z}_{rnd})$  in  $U_2$ ): The game simulates the proof  $(\widetilde{A}_{rnd}, \widetilde{c}_{rnd}, \widetilde{z}_{rnd})$  instead of computing it honestly in  $U_2$ . That is, the game samples  $c_{rnd} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and sets  $(\widetilde{A}_{rnd}, \widetilde{z}_{rnd}) \leftarrow \Sigma_{rnd}.Sim(\mathbb{X}_{rnd}, \widetilde{c}_{rnd})$ . Further, it programs H such that  $H(in_H) = (\cdot, \cdot, \widetilde{c}_{rnd})$  in the last component, where  $in_H$  is defined as in  $G_1$  above. Else, it proceeds as  $G_2$ .

Note that the output of H on input  $in_H$  changes between  $U_1$  and  $U_2$ . However, due to the abort condition introduced in  $G_1$ , this change is not noticeable by the adversary and the H outputs are identically distributed in the view of A. Further, note that  $(x_{rnd}, w_{rnd}) \in \mathfrak{R}_{rnd}$  by construction. Thus, by SHVZK of  $\Sigma_{rnd}$ , the  $\Sigma$ -protocol transcripts are identically distributed. We have

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_1^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_2^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

Game G<sub>3</sub> (Simulate the OR-proof): Instead of randomizing the transcripts  $(A_{\text{dleq}}, c_{\text{dleq}}, z_{\text{dleq}})$  and  $(A'_{\text{mac}}, c_{\text{mac}}, z'_{\text{mac}})$  in both U<sub>1</sub> and U<sub>2</sub>, the game simulates the OR-proof for  $\mathfrak{L}_{\text{mac}} \cup \mathfrak{L}_{\text{dleq}}$  and programs H appropriately. Here, the transcript  $(A'_{\text{mac}}, c_{\text{mac}}, z'_{\text{mac}})$  denotes the adversarially-issued  $\Sigma_{\text{mac}}$  transcript after applying the modifications marked with in Figure 6, but before the other blinding operations are applied.

In more detail, the game sends a random challenge  $c_{\sf or} \leftarrow {}^{\$}\mathbb{Z}_p$  instead of  $\widetilde{c}_{\sf or} - \gamma_{\sf mac} - \gamma_{\sf dleq}$  in U<sub>1</sub>. Further, it simulates the proofs  $(\widetilde{A}_{\sf dleq}, \widetilde{c}_{\sf dleq}, \widetilde{c}_{\sf dleq})$  and  $(\widetilde{A}_{\sf mac}, \widetilde{c}_{\sf mac}, \widetilde{z}_{\sf mac})$  in U<sub>2</sub>. That is, in U<sub>2</sub>, the game samples  $\widetilde{c}_{\sf dleq}, \widetilde{c}_{\sf or} \leftarrow {}^{\$}\mathbb{Z}_p$  and sets  $\widetilde{c}_{\sf mac} \leftarrow \widetilde{c}_{\sf or} - \widetilde{c}_{\sf dleq}$ . Then, it computes  $(\widetilde{A}_{\sf dleq}, \widetilde{z}_{\sf dleq}) \leftarrow \Sigma_{\sf dleq}. \mathsf{Sim}(\mathbb{x}_{\sf dleq}, \widetilde{c}_{\sf dleq})$  and  $(\widetilde{A}_{\sf mac}, \widetilde{z}_{\sf mac}) \leftarrow \Sigma_{\sf mac}. \mathsf{Sim}(\mathbb{x}'_{\sf mac}, \widetilde{c}_{\sf mac})$ . Finally, it programs H such that  $\mathsf{H}(\mathsf{in}_\mathsf{H}) = (\cdot, \widetilde{c}_{\sf or}, \cdot)$  in the second component, where  $\mathsf{in}_\mathsf{H}$  is defined as in  $\mathbf{G}_1$ .

Observe that in  $\mathbf{G}_2$ , the transcripts  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{dleq}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{dleq}})$  and  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{mac}})$  are obtained from  $(A_{\mathsf{dleq}}, c_{\mathsf{dleq}}, z_{\mathsf{dleq}})$  and  $(A'_{\mathsf{mac}}, c_{\mathsf{mac}}, z'_{\mathsf{mac}})$  by the randomization algorithm from Lemma 2.18, respectively. Also, note that the modified  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  transcript  $(A'_{\mathsf{mac}}, c_{\mathsf{mac}}, z'_{\mathsf{mac}})$  verifies if  $(A_{\mathsf{mac}}, c_{\mathsf{mac}}, z_{\mathsf{mac}})$  verifies, as shown in section 5. As  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  and  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  have strongly randomizable transcripts, the simulated transcripts are distributed identically to the randomized transcripts (cf. Corollary 2.17). It remains to argue that the oracle H is identically distributed in the view of A. This follows by the abort condition introduced in  $\mathbf{G}_1$  and as  $\widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{or}}$  is identically distributed in both games.

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_2^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_3^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

{49}------------------------------------------------

Game  $G_4$  (Simulate  $(\widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{os}, \widetilde{z}_{os})$  in  $U_2$ ): Instead of randomizing the transcripts  $(A_{os}, c_{os}, z_{os})$  in both  $U_1$  and  $U_2$ , the game simulates the proof  $(\widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{os}, \widetilde{z}_{os})$  and programs H appropriately. That is, the game sends a random challenge  $c \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  instead of  $\widetilde{c}_{os} - \gamma_{os}$  in  $U_1$ . Further, it simulates  $(\widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{z}_{os}) \leftarrow \Sigma_{os}.Sim(\mathbb{X}_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{os})$  in  $U_2$  for  $\widetilde{c}_{os} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and programs H such that  $H(\mathsf{in}_\mathsf{H}) = (\widetilde{c}_{os}, \cdot, \cdot)$  in the first component, where  $\mathsf{in}_\mathsf{H}$  is defined as in  $G_1$ .

Observe that in  $\mathbf{G}_3$ , the transcript  $(\widetilde{A}_{os}, \widetilde{c}_{os}, \widetilde{z}_{os})$  is obtained from  $(A_{os}, c_{os}, z_{os})$  by the randomization algorithm from Lemma 2.18. As  $\Sigma_{os}$  has strongly randomizable transcripts, the simulated transcript is distributed identical to the randomized transcript (cf. Corollary 2.17). Furthermore, the oracle H is identically distributed in the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  by the abort condition introduced in  $\mathbf{G}_1$ .

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_3^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

Game  $G_5$  (Commit to zero in cmt<sub>rnd</sub>): The game now commits to the zero vector over  $\mathbb{G}^7$  in cmt<sub>rnd</sub>. As the opening is not required anymore as witness in the  $\Sigma_{rnd}$  proof, it is straightforward to show that there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  such that

$$|\Pr[\mathbf{G}_4^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \Pr[\mathbf{G}_5^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| = 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{hide}}_{\mathsf{Cond}}(\mathcal{B}, \lambda).$$

Note that all following game hops are statistical. We note that  $G_6$  and  $G_7$  are inefficient.

Game G<sub>6</sub> (Abort if  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  is dishonest): The game (inefficiently) brute-forces the mac key  $\mathsf{msk} = (x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z, \rho_0)$  and verifies that the obtained  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}}$  in U<sub>1</sub> is honestly computed. That is, the game parses the issuer parameters ipp from  $\mathsf{pk}$  as  $\mathsf{ipp} = (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z)$  and computes  $x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z$  and  $\rho_0$  such that  $\mathsf{cmt}_0 = \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Commit( $\mathsf{mck}, (x_0, y_0); \rho_0$ ),  $X_1 = x_1 F, Y_1 = y_1 F$  and Z = z F. In U<sub>1</sub>, the game parses  $\sigma_{\mathsf{mac}} = (U, V, S, T)$ , brute-forces  $u \in \mathbb{Z}_p^*$  such that U = u G and checks that  $V = z U, S = u(x_0 G + x_1 A_{\mathsf{os}})$  and  $T = u(y_0 G + y_1 A_{\mathsf{os}})$ . If a check fails, the game aborts, else the game proceeds as before.

Note that the game aborts iff  $\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac}} = (\mathsf{ipp}, M, U, V, S, T, 0, 0) \notin \mathfrak{L}_{\mathsf{mac}}$  as  $\phi_{\mathsf{pp}, \mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac}}}^{\mathsf{mac}}$  is injective (i.e., the brute-forced witness  $\mathsf{msk}$  is unique) by perfect strong binding of  $\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}$ . Also, observe that as there are at most  $Q_{\mathsf{pb}}$  queries to  $\mathsf{H}_{\mathsf{pb}}$ , the tuple  $\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}} = (D_1, D_2, D_3)$  is not a DDH-tuple (i.e.,  $\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}} \notin \mathfrak{L}_{\mathsf{dleq}}$ ) except with probability  $Q_{\mathsf{pb}}/p$ . In total, if an abort occurs, then  $\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{mac}} \notin \mathfrak{L}_{\mathsf{mac}}$  and  $\mathbb{x}_{\mathsf{dleq}} \notin \mathfrak{L}_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  except with probability  $Q_{\mathsf{pb}}/p$ . Further, the adversary provides  $A_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  and  $A_{\mathsf{mac}}$  in  $\mathsf{U}_1$ . By special soundness of  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{dleq}}$  and  $\mathcal{L}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$ , there is at most a single challenge pair  $(c_{\mathsf{dleq}}, c_{\mathsf{mac}})$  such that there exists responses  $(z_{\mathsf{dleq}}, z_{\mathsf{mac}})$  that complete the  $\mathcal{L}$ -protocol transcripts (such that both transcripts verify). The probability that  $c_{\mathsf{or}} = c_{\mathsf{dleq}} + c_{\mathsf{mac}}$  is at most 1/p and since there are at most two non-aborting  $\mathsf{U}_1$  calls in total, we obtain

$$\left| \Pr[\mathbf{G}_5^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \Pr[\mathbf{G}_6^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] \right| \leqslant \frac{Q_{\mathsf{pb}} + 2}{p}.$$

Game G<sub>7</sub> (Compute  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}$  independently from  $\sigma_{mac}$ ): The game computes the blinded MAC  $\widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}$  and the blinded message  $\widetilde{M}$  as follows

$$u \leftarrow_{\$} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{*}$$
,  $\widetilde{M} \leftarrow_{\$} \mathbb{G}^{*}$ ,  $\widetilde{M} \leftarrow_{\$} \mathbb{G}^{*}$ ,  $\widetilde{U} \leftarrow uG$ ,  $\widetilde{V} \leftarrow uzG$ ,  $\widetilde{S}_{1} \leftarrow_{\$} \mathbb{G}$ ,  $\widetilde{S}_{0} \leftarrow u(x_{0}G + x_{1}\widetilde{M} - \widetilde{S}_{1})$ ,  $\widetilde{T}_{1} \leftarrow_{\$} \mathbb{G}$ ,  $\widetilde{T}_{0} \leftarrow u(y_{0}G + y_{1}\widetilde{M} - \widetilde{T}_{1})$ ,

where  $\mathsf{msk} = (x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z, \rho_0)$  is as in  $\mathbf{G}_6$ . Note that this is possible because the transcripts  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{mac}})$  and  $(\widetilde{A}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{c}_{\mathsf{rnd}}, \widetilde{z}_{\mathsf{rnd}})$  are simulated and the commitment  $\mathsf{cmt}_{\mathsf{rnd}}$  commits to the zero vector.

It is easy to see that  $(\widetilde{\sigma}_{\mathsf{mac}}, \widetilde{M})$  is identically distributed in  $\mathbf{G}_6$  and  $\mathbf{G}_7$  due to the abort condition introduced in  $\mathbf{G}_6$ . That is, in  $\mathbf{G}_6$ , we have  $u \in \mathbb{Z}_p^*$  such that U = uG and  $V = zU, S = u(x_0G + x_1A_{\mathsf{os}})$  and

{50}------------------------------------------------

 $T = u(y_0G + y_1A_{os})$ . Further,  $(\widetilde{\sigma}_{mac}, \widetilde{M})$  is computed from (U, V, S, T) and  $A_{os}$  as follows

$$\beta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{*}, \quad r_{x}, r_{y}, r_{M} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p} , \qquad \qquad \widetilde{M} \leftarrow A_{os} + r_{M}F ,$$

$$\widetilde{U} \leftarrow \beta U , \qquad \qquad \widetilde{V} \leftarrow \beta V ,$$

$$\widetilde{S}_{1} \leftarrow r_{x}G + r_{M}X_{1} , \qquad \qquad \widetilde{S}_{0} \leftarrow \beta S - r_{x}\widetilde{U} ,$$

$$\widetilde{T}_{1} \leftarrow r_{y}G + r_{M}Y_{1} , \qquad \qquad \widetilde{T}_{0} \leftarrow \beta T - r_{y}\widetilde{U} .$$

Recall that  $x_1F = X_1$  and  $y_1F = Y_1$ . The claim follows since the values  $\widetilde{M}$ ,  $\widetilde{U} = (\beta u)G$ ,  $\widetilde{V} = (\beta uz)G$  in  $\mathbf{G}_6$  trivially follow the distribution from  $\mathbf{G}_7$  and further, in  $\mathbf{G}_6$  we have

$$\beta u(x_0G + x_1\widetilde{M} - \widetilde{S}_1) = \beta u(x_0G + x_1(A_{os} + r_MF) - r_xG - r_M(x_1F))$$

$$= \beta u(x_0G + x_1A_{os} - r_xG)$$

$$= \beta S - r_x\widetilde{U}$$

$$= \widetilde{S}_0$$

so also  $(\widetilde{S}_0, \widetilde{S}_1)$  follow the distribution from  $\mathbf{G}_7$ , and similarly for  $(\widetilde{T}_0, \widetilde{T}_1)$ . In total, we obtain

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_6^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \Pr[\mathbf{G}_7^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1].$$

ADVANTAGE OF  $\mathcal{A}$  IN  $\mathbf{G}_7$ . Observe that the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  in  $\mathbf{G}_7$  is independent from the bit b sampled by the game. Thus, we have b = b' with probability 1/2, therefore

$$\Pr[\mathbf{G}_7^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] = \frac{1}{2}.$$

The claim follows by collecting all bounds.
