### <span id="page-54-0"></span>A Proof of Lemma 2.6

Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be the adversary running in time  $T_{\mathcal{A}} = T_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda)$  and making  $Q_{S_1} = Q_{S_1}(\lambda), Q_{S_2} = Q_{S_2}(\lambda)$  to  $S_1, S_2$ , respectively. We consider the following adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  simulating the OMUF/OMSUF game to  $\mathcal{A}$  while playing the OMUF/OMSUF game itself.

Parameters and key. The adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  takes as input (pp, vk) from the game and forwards them to  $\mathcal{A}$ . Signing oracle  $S_1$ . When  $\mathcal{A}$  makes a query info to  $S_1$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  forwards the query to its own  $S_1$  oracle, while keeping track of the counter cnt of the number of sessions opened and set  $\mathsf{info}_{\mathsf{cnt}} \leftarrow \mathsf{info}$ . Then, forward the output  $\mathsf{smsg}_{1,\mathsf{cnt}}$  from the oracle to  $\mathcal{A}$ .

Signing oracle  $S_2$ . When  $\mathcal{A}$  makes a query (sid, umsg) to  $S_2$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  forwards the query to  $S_2$ . Then, forwards the output  $\mathsf{smsg}_{2,\mathrm{sid}}$  back to  $\mathcal{A}$ .

**Finishing opened sessions.** When  $\mathcal{A}$  returns the forgeries  $(\inf^*, (\mu^{(i)}, \sigma^{(i)})_{i \in [\ell]})$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  finishes the unclosed sessions as follows. For each sid such that  $\mathcal{A}$  does not make  $S_2$  query on,

- (a) Pick  $\mu_{\text{sid}}$  such that  $\mu_{\text{sid}} \notin \{\mu^{(i)}\}_{i \in [\ell]}$  and  $\mathcal{B}$  has not used  $\mu_{\text{sid}}$  to finish a session before,
- (b) Compute  $(\mathsf{umsg}_{\mathrm{sid}}, \mathsf{st}_{\mathrm{sid}}^u) \leftarrow \mathsf{sBS}_{\mathrm{alg}}. \bar{\mathsf{U}}_1(\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{vk}, \mathsf{info}_{\mathrm{sid}}, \mu_{\mathrm{sid}}, \mathsf{smsg}_{1,\mathrm{sid}}),$
- (c) Query  $smsg_{2,sid} \leftarrow S_2(sid, umsg_{sid})$ , and
- (d) Compute  $\sigma_{\text{sid}}^* \leftarrow \mathsf{BS}_{\text{alg}}.\mathsf{U}_2(\mathsf{smsg}_{2,\text{sid}},\mathsf{st}_{\text{sid}}^u)$ .

Forgery. Let S be the set of sid with  $\inf o^* = \inf o_{\operatorname{sid}}$  and  $\mathcal{B}$  closes the signing sessions in the previous step. Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  returns  $(\inf o^*, (\mu^{(i)}, \sigma^{(i)})_{i \in [\ell]} \cup (\mu_{\operatorname{sid}}, \sigma^*_{\operatorname{sid}})_{\operatorname{sid} \in S})$ 

Note that by correctness of  $\mathsf{BS}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  the pairs  $(\mu_{\mathsf{sid}}, \sigma^*_{\mathsf{sid}})_{\mathsf{sid} \in S}$  are valid signatures with respect to  $\mathsf{pp}, \mathsf{vk}$  and  $\mathsf{info}^*$ . Thus, if  $\mathcal{A}$  wins in OMUF/OMSUF game,  $\mathcal{B}$  wins as well, implying the advantage bound. Accordingly, the query count for  $\mathcal{B}$  is exactly  $Q_{\mathsf{S}_1}$  for both oracles and the running time of  $\mathcal{B}$  is roughly that of  $\mathcal{A}$ .  $\square$ 

### <span id="page-54-1"></span>B Proof of Lemma 2.20

We first recall the splitting lemma in the version used in [BCJ08]. Our proof resembles that of [BCJ08] except that we do not rewind for multiple times per index, but only once.

**Lemma B.1 (Splitting Lemma [BCJ08]).** Let  $A, B, S \subseteq \mathcal{X} \times \mathcal{Y}$ ,  $A \subseteq S$  with Pr[S] > 0, and  $B := \{(x,y) : Pr_{y' \leftrightarrow \mathcal{Y}}[(x,y') \in A] \ge \delta\}$  for  $\delta \in [0,1]$ . Then,

1.  $\Pr[A \cap B] \geqslant \Pr[A] - \delta$ 2.  $\Pr[A \cap B|S] \geqslant \Pr[A|S] - \delta/\Pr[S]$ 

We first consider the following sets of inputs (inp,  $\rho$ , h) of A where inp  $\in$  [IG()],  $\rho$  is the random coins of A, and  $h \in C^Q$ .

- $\mathcal{S} := \{(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, h) : \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{inp}, h; \rho) \neq \bot\}$  be the set of inputs where  $\mathcal{A}$  succeeds.
- For each  $i \in [Q]$ , let  $\mathcal{W}_i := \{(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}) : (I, \mathsf{aux}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho), i \in I\} = \bigcup_{j \in \{0,1\}} W_i^j$  be the set of inputs where the output of  $\mathcal{A}$  contains index i.
- For each  $j \in \{0,1\}, i \in [Q]$ , let  $\mathcal{W}_i^j := \{(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}) : (I, \mathsf{aux}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(\mathsf{inp}, \boldsymbol{h}; \rho); i = I_j\} \subseteq \mathcal{S}$  be the set of inputs where the j-th position of the output I of  $\mathcal{A}$  is i.
- For each  $i \in [Q]$ , let  $\mathsf{Heavy}_i := \{(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}) : \mathsf{Pr}_{\boldsymbol{h}'_{[i:Q]}} \in \mathcal{C}^{Q-i+1}[(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}_{1:i-1} \| \boldsymbol{h}'_{[i:Q]}) \in \mathcal{W}_i] \geqslant \delta \}$ . Here,  $\mathsf{Heavy}_i$  defines the set of inputs where after forking at index i, the forked run outputs index i.
- Accordingly, for each  $j \in \{0, 1\}, i \in [Q]$ , let

$$\mathsf{Heavy}_i^j := \{(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}) : \mathsf{Pr}_{\boldsymbol{h}'_{[i:Q]}} \mathrel{\hookleftarrow} \mathcal{C}^{Q-i+1}[(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}_{1:i-1} \| \boldsymbol{h}'_{[i:Q]}) \in \mathcal{W}_i^j] \geqslant \delta \} \; .$$

Note that since  $W_i^j \subseteq W_i$ , we can see that  $\mathsf{Heavy}_i^j \subseteq \mathsf{Heavy}_i$ .

• For each  $j \in \{0,1\}$ , let  $E_j = \bigcup_{i \in [Q]} (\mathcal{W}_i^j \cap \mathsf{Heavy}_i) \subseteq \mathcal{S}$  be the set of inputs that for the j-th position  $I_j$  of the output of  $\mathcal{A}$ , the input is in  $\mathsf{Heavy}_{I_j}$ .

{55}------------------------------------------------

The general proof strategy is that if the first run of  $\mathcal{A}$  within Fork<sub>3</sub> leads to the input that is in  $E = E_0 \cap E_1$ , the latter runs are much likelier to result in the forking. In particular, we have that

$$\begin{split} & \text{frk} = \mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp},\rho} \left[ \begin{array}{l} (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h') \in \mathcal{S} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_1} \land \\ h'_{l_f} \neq h_{l_0} \land h'_{l_1} \neq h_{l_1} \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_1} \land \\ h'_{l_f} \neq h_{l_0} \land h'_{l_1} \neq h_{l_1} \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_1} \land \\ h'_{l_0} \neq h_{l_0} \land h'_{l_1} \neq h_{l_1} \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_1} \land \\ h'_{l_0} \neq h_{l_0} \land h'_{l_1} \neq h_{l_1} \\ h'_{l_1:Q} = \mathsf{sc} \, \mathcal{C}^{Q-l_0+1} : h' = h_{[1:l_0-1]} |h'_{[l_0:Q]} \\ & + \mathcal{C}(\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_1} \land h'_{l_1} \neq h_{l_1} \\ h''_{l_0:Q} = \mathsf{sc} \, \mathcal{C}^{Q-l_0+1} : h' = h_{[1:l_0-1]} |h'_{[l_0:Q]} \\ & + \mathcal{C}(\mathsf{inp},\rho,h') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ h'_{l_0} \neq h_{l_0} \land h'_{l_1} \neq h_{l_1} \\ h''_{l_0:Q} = \mathsf{sc} \, \mathcal{C}^{Q-l_0+1} : h' = h_{[1:l_0-1]} |h'_{[l_0:Q]} \\ & + \mathcal{C}(\mathsf{inp},\rho,h') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,h'') \in \mathcal{W}_{l_0} \land \\ (\mathsf{inp}$$

The first line is by definition of frk and Fork<sub>3</sub>. The second line is by  $E \subseteq \mathcal{S}$ . The third line is by conditional probability. The fourth line is by law of total probability over all the possible values of  $I_0, I_1$  (here, we also use shorthand Pr[E] to denote (inp,  $\rho, h$ )  $\in E$ ). The fifth line is only rewriting the probability notation and that  $I_0 = i_0, I_1 = i_1$ . The last equality is due to conditional probability.

Note that for  $(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}) \in E \cap W^0_{i_0} \cap W^1_{i_1}$ , we have that  $(\mathsf{inp}, \rho, \boldsymbol{h}) \in \mathsf{Heavy}_{i_0} \cap \mathsf{Heavy}_{i_1}$  by definition of E. Therefore, by definition of  $\mathsf{Heavy}_i$ ,

$$\mathsf{Pr}_{\mathsf{inp},\rho,\boldsymbol{h},\boldsymbol{h}',\boldsymbol{h}''} \left[ \begin{array}{c} (\mathsf{inp},\rho,\boldsymbol{h}') \in \mathcal{W}_{i_0} \wedge \\ (\mathsf{inp},\rho,\boldsymbol{h}'') \in \mathcal{W}_{i_1} \wedge \\ h'_{I_0} \neq h_{I_0} \wedge h''_{I_1} \neq h_{I_1} \end{array} \right| \begin{pmatrix} (\mathsf{inp},\rho,\boldsymbol{h}) \in E \cap W^0_{i_0} \cap W^1_{i_1} \\ \boldsymbol{h}'_{[1:i_0-1]} = \boldsymbol{h}_{[1:i_0-1]} \\ \boldsymbol{h}''_{[1:i_1-1]} = \boldsymbol{h}_{[1:i_1-1]} \end{array} \right] \geqslant \left(\delta - \frac{1}{|\mathcal{C}|}\right)^2 \ .$$

Therefore, we can lower bound the sum as  $(\delta - 1/|\mathcal{C}|)^2$ .

Finally, we lower bound Pr[E].

$$\Pr[E] = \Pr[S] \Pr[E|S] = \operatorname{accPr}[E_0 \cap E_1|S]$$

{56}------------------------------------------------

$$\geqslant \operatorname{acc}(1 - \sum_{j \in \{0,1\}} \Pr[\neg E_j | \mathcal{S}])$$

Thus, we now upper bound  $\Pr[\neg E_j | \mathcal{S}]$ , or equivalently, lower bound  $\Pr[E_j | \mathcal{S}]$ . In particular, we claim that  $\Pr[E_j | \mathcal{S}] \geqslant 1 - Q\delta \cdot \mathsf{acc}^{-1}$ . Here, observe that  $\mathcal{W}_i^j$  are disjoint for  $i \in [Q]$ , meaning

$$\begin{split} \Pr[E_j|\mathcal{S}] &= \sum_{i \in [Q]} \Pr[\mathcal{W}_i^j \cap \mathsf{Heavy}_i|\mathcal{S}] \\ &\geqslant \sum_{i \in [Q]} \Pr[\mathcal{W}_i^j \cap \mathsf{Heavy}_i^j|\mathcal{S}] \\ &\geqslant \sum_{i \in [Q]} \Pr[\mathcal{W}_i^j|\mathcal{S}] - \delta \Pr[\mathcal{S}]^{-1} \\ &1 - Q\delta \cdot \mathsf{acc}^{-1} \;. \end{split}$$

The second line follows from  $\mathsf{Heavy}_i^j \subseteq \mathsf{Heavy}_i$ . The third line follows from the splitting lemma. The final line follows from  $\mathcal{S} = \bigcup_{i \in [Q]} \mathcal{W}_i^j$  since at index j,  $I_j$  needs to take on exactly one value from [Q]. Finally, setting  $\delta = \frac{\mathsf{acc}}{4Q}$ , we have that

$$\begin{split} \operatorname{frk} &\geqslant \Pr[E] \left( \delta - \frac{1}{|\mathcal{C}|} \right)^2 \\ &\geqslant \operatorname{acc}(1 - \sum_{j \in \{0,1\}} \Pr[\neg E_j | \mathcal{S}]) \left( \frac{\operatorname{acc}}{4Q} - \frac{1}{|\mathcal{C}|} \right)^2 \\ &\geqslant \operatorname{acc}(1 - 2Q\delta \cdot \operatorname{acc}^{-1}) \left( \frac{\operatorname{acc}}{4Q} - \frac{1}{|\mathcal{C}|} \right)^2 \\ &\geqslant \frac{\operatorname{acc}}{2} \left( \frac{\operatorname{acc}}{4Q} - \frac{1}{|\mathcal{C}|} \right)^2 \;. \end{split}$$

Therefore, we have that  $\operatorname{frk} \geqslant \frac{1}{32Q^2} \left(\operatorname{acc} - \frac{4Q}{|\mathcal{C}|}\right)^3$ , which implies that  $\operatorname{acc} \leqslant \sqrt[3]{32Q^2 \cdot \operatorname{frk}} + \frac{4Q}{|\mathcal{C}|}$ .

Remark B.2. We only state the lemma for 2-index forking. However, we can extend the proof to the case where  $I \in [Q]^{\ell}$  for  $\ell \leq Q$  instead of  $\ell = 2$  with similar techniques. In particular, the bound becomes

$$\operatorname{frk} \geqslant \frac{\operatorname{acc}}{2} \left( \frac{\operatorname{acc}}{2\ell Q} - \frac{1}{|\mathcal{C}|} \right)^{\ell} .$$

### <span id="page-56-0"></span>C Proof of Theorem 3.1

We give the simple proof for the algebraic MAC for the self-containment of the paper. Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be an adversary making at most Q Tag-oracle queries. At the end of the game, it outputs  $(m^*, \sigma_{\text{alg}}^*)$  and wins if  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}.\mathsf{Ver}(\mathsf{mpp},\mathsf{ipp},\mathsf{msk},m^*,\sigma_{\mathsf{alg}}^*)=1$ . Then, we consider the following sequence of games  $\mathbf{G}_0,\mathbf{G}_1$ .

Game G<sub>0</sub> (Original game.): This is the original UF-RMA game for  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  such that  $\mathsf{mpp} = (F, \mathsf{mck})$ , where  $F \leftarrow \mathsf{s} \, \mathbb{G}$  and  $\mathsf{mck} \leftarrow \mathsf{s} \, \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ , the issuer's public parameters  $\mathsf{ipp} = (\mathsf{cmt}_0, X_1, Y_1, Z)$  computed from the secret key  $\mathsf{msk} = (x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z, \rho)$  as

$${\rm cmt}_0 = {\sf C}_{\sf mac}.{\sf Commit}({\sf mck},(x_0,y_0);\rho), X_1 = x_1F, Y_1 = y_1F, Z = zF$$

Game  $G_1$  (cmt<sub>0</sub> commits to (0,0).): In this game, cmt<sub>0</sub> is now  $C_{mac}$ .Commit(mck, (0,0);  $\rho$ ) for  $\rho \leftarrow C_{mac}$ . $\mathcal{R}$  instead. We can argue that

$$|\mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_0^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1] - \mathsf{Pr}[\mathbf{G}_1^{\mathcal{A}} \Rightarrow 1]| \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{hide}}_{\mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}}(\mathcal{B}_1, \lambda) \;,$$

{57}------------------------------------------------

by constructing  $\mathcal{B}_1$  which picks two messages to be committed  $(x_0, y_0) \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^2$  and (0, 0). When  $\mathcal{B}_1$  receives  $\mathrm{cmt}_0$ , it simulates Tag as in the original game using  $(x_0, x_1, y_0, y_1, z)$ . At the end of the game, output 1 if  $\mathcal{A}$  returns a valid forgery; otherwise output 0. The reduction does not need  $\rho$  to simulate the Tag oracle nor the verification at the end. This is by how  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ . Tag and  $\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ . Ver are defined. Thus, we have shown the advantage change. Note that  $\mathcal{B}_1$  runs in time roughly  $T_{\mathcal{A}}$ .

Finally, we refer to [CAHLT25, Theorem 6.1] adapted to UF-RMA security. The original theorem proves the stronger UF-CMVA security of  $M'_{alg}$ , which is  $M_{alg}$  without the commitment cmt<sub>0</sub>.

Theorem C.1 (Theorem 6.1 of [CAHLT25] adapted). Let GGen be a group parameters generator outputting groups of prime-order  $p = p(\lambda)$ ,  $M'_{alg} = M'_{alg}[GGen]$  be the algebraic MAC scheme identical to  $M_{alg}$  except that mpp does not contain mck and ipp does not contain cmt<sub>0</sub>. For any A running in time  $T_A = T_A(\lambda)$  and making at most  $Q = Q(\lambda)$  queries to the Tag oracle, there exist adversaries  $\mathcal{B}$  running in time  $\approx T_A$  such that

$$\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ufrma}}_{\mathsf{M}_{\mathsf{alg}}'}(\mathcal{A},\lambda) \leqslant Q \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ddh}}_{\mathsf{GGen}}(\mathcal{B},\lambda) + \frac{3}{p} \;.$$

Our final reduction  $\mathcal{B}_2$  can simulate the game  $\mathbf{G}_1$  to  $\mathcal{A}$  by computing  $\mathrm{cmt}_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{C}_{\mathsf{mac}}.\mathsf{Commit}(\mathsf{mck}, (0,0); \rho)$ , forwarding other elements in  $\mathsf{mpp}$  and  $\mathsf{ipp}$  of  $\mathsf{M}'_{\mathsf{alg}}$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ , Tag is simulated by delegating to its own Tag oracle, and  $\mathcal{A}$ 's forgery is  $\mathcal{B}_2$ 's forgery to its UFRMA game. Therefore, we have the bound as in Theorem 3.1.  $\square$
